Steamboat Stewards Take Joint Responsibility Guarantee; Resolution of the Steamboat Industry Association

Steamboat stewards often carry smuggled goods, evading not only customs duties but also freight charges. Since the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company first rectified the smuggling of small packages last year, annual revenue has increased by over 100,000 yuan. Furthermore, the Jianghai Customs has thoroughly investigated stewards' private carrying of goods, strictly stipulating fines and requiring the steamboat companies to be responsible. If smuggled highly poisonous materials are discovered, the penalty is death. After the promulgation of this regulation, steamboat companies, burdened with excessive responsibility, worried that unscrupulous stewards might engage in such activities, and once a case is cracked or a steward escapes, the steamboat companies would be unable to bear such a heavy responsibility. The steamboat companies submitted this case to the Municipal Shipping Association for discussion. The association has resolved that all steamboat stewards must take joint responsibility guarantee. Those already employed must submit supplementary joint responsibility guarantee forms, and the association will notify all steamboat companies to implement this uniformly. The original proposal is recorded below: "To all members, according to statements from member companies, since the Customs announced that 'seafarers and stewards carrying smuggled goods will be fined from 200 to 1,000 yuan, to be borne by the steamboat companies,' and Chairman Chiang issued Article 2 of the regulations strictly prohibiting highly poisonous materials, which states 'those who manufacture or transport highly poisonous materials will be sentenced to death,' the matter is extremely serious. If any seafarers or stewards carry such materials due to the lure of high profits, and the matter is exposed, the seafarers and stewards are employees of the steamboat companies. If the main culprit is at large, the companies must be investigated, which is an unbearable burden. To prevent such occurrences and reduce responsibility, a sound plan must be devised. Please devise a guarantee method.' The proposal was submitted to the 29th Executive Committee meeting on the 15th of this month, and it was resolved that 'the association should notify all members to adopt the joint responsibility guarantee method for seafarers and stewards to provide security and facilitate mutual supervision.' This record is issued as a notification, and we hope you will comply and not misinterpret. Sincerely, The Shanghai Steamboat Industry Association, March 18th."

103 Chinese Ships Involved in Accidents Last Year; Ministry of Transportation Orders Shipping Companies to Carefully Select Crew Members; Collisions Account for the Majority of Accidents; 15 Ships Hijacked by Pirates

Last year, 103 Chinese ships were involved in accidents, and 70-80% of them were ships sailing to and from Shanghai, setting a record unseen in the shipping industry in recent years. This resulted in significant losses for ship insurance companies last year. The Ministry of Transportation has summarized the causes of the accidents involving the 103 ships and issued instructions to Shanghai, noting that collisions accounted for the majority of accidents, including Hongxing, Tonghua, Xinrenhe, Tongshang, Puan, and 25 others. The most tragic incident was a small ship in Fuzhou where over 40 passengers died. Eight ships ran aground, including Fulong, Yuanshun, Jinglong, Tianxiang, and others. Sunken ships included Zhaoxing, Fuyuan, Yuli, Xinhongyuan, Haiping, and others. Fires occurred on Huitong, Daqing, Xingshi, Xinfeng, Ruihua, and others. Fifteen ships were hijacked by pirates, including Puan, Xinbaohe, Linpu, Yaobei, Shunfa, Chuanshan, Lishun, He'an, Jiahe, Xinhaiwen, Hengji, Daishan, Tongan, Tailai, and Longsheng. Groundings and engine failures were even more frequent. The accidents, sinkings, and pirate attacks involving foreign ships are not included. In summary, the accidents involving merchant ships are mainly due to natural disasters and human error. The dereliction of duty of crew members is particularly numerous. Learning from the past and being mindful of future disasters, the ministry has ordered all shipping companies to pay special attention to the skills of the crew members they hire and not to allow unqualified individuals to fill positions, leading to tragedies at sea.

Central Mint Ordered to Temporarily Suspend Minting Bullion; Expedite Minting of New Coins to Meet Market Demand

The Central Mint was ordered by the Ministry of Finance to temporarily suspend the minting of types A and B of 880 and 999 bullion bars from the 9th of this month and to expedite the minting of new coins to meet market demand. The mint now mints new coins every day that are tested and certified, then delivered to the Central Bank for distribution. The daily output is approximately 300,000 to 400,000 yuan. The date to resume minting bullion bars will depend on market conditions. 3,621 type A bullion bars and 51,640 type B bars have already been minted, each bar worth 1,000 silver dollars.

1933 Customs Treasury Bill Exchange Method; Can Entrust Central Bank and Other Banks to Exchange

The Ministry of Finance believes that the number of 10,000 yuan Customs Treasury Bills from 1933 is very large. To facilitate circulation, it has formulated a method for exchanging 10,000 yuan bills for 1,000 yuan bills. The Ministry of Finance will issue a public announcement and begin implementing the method on the 26th of this month. The following is an excerpt of the method:

Ministry of Finance Announcement

Announcement No. 84 of the Ministry of Finance states: "To facilitate the circulation of the 1933 Customs Treasury Bills, the Ministry has approved the exchange of 10,000 yuan bills for 1,000 yuan bills and designated the Shanghai office of the Ministry's Public Debt Division at 452 Jiangxi Road to be responsible for managing the exchange. The method will be published in the newspaper on March 26, 1935 for public awareness. This announcement is hereby made."

Exchange Method

(1) To facilitate circulation, the Ministry of Finance approves the exchange of 10,000 yuan bills for 1,000 yuan bills and assigns the Public Debt Division's Shanghai office to be responsible for managing the exchange. (2) The Ministry of Finance originally printed 2,000 10,000 yuan bills for a total face value of 20,000,000 yuan. 20,000 1,000 yuan bills will be reprinted with a total face value of 20,000,000 yuan, numbered from A00001 to A20000, for holders to exchange. (3) The Ministry of Finance will publish a notice in the newspaper that all holders of the 10,000 yuan Customs Treasury Bills may exchange one 10,000 yuan bill for ten 1,000 yuan bills at the designated exchange office within the prescribed time limit. (4) For 10,000 yuan bills circulating in various locations, the exchange office will send letters to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in various locations, requesting that they forward any bills submitted by holders to the Shanghai office for processing. The postage fees will be paid by the holders. (5) The exchange office will list the amount of bills exchanged daily, report them in detail, punch holes in the exchanged bills to invalidate them, and record the last two digits of the serial number for submission to the National Debt Foundation for record keeping. (6) The exchange office will store the 10,000 yuan bills collected daily in the custody of the Gold Management Committee. After accumulating a sufficient amount, the office will request that the Ministry of Finance send personnel to inspect and destroy them. (7) The Ministry of Finance may amend or supplement this method at any time if there are any omissions.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Writes to Niter and Sulfur Bureau; Requesting Compliance with the Flying Flowers Purchase Sulfur Agreement

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce wrote to the Jiangsu Niter and Sulfur Bureau and the Niter and Sulfur Transportation and Sales Office yesterday regarding the issue of flying flower factories purchasing niter and sulfur: "Previously, flying flower factories needed niter and sulfur and would apply for passports to purchase it themselves. Later, the requirement was changed to purchase it through the Niter and Sulfur Bureau. Our association submitted a petition and obtained approval No. 169 from the Ministry of Military Affairs, allowing our association to be responsible for providing certification and submitting it to the ministry for passport issuance." As the Jiangsu Provincial Niter and Sulfur Transportation and Sales Office believed this matter would hinder their business, they asked our association to mediate. If the industry could purchase it through them, they were willing to reduce their profits. Therefore, based on this principle, our association's former chairman Wang Maolai, the Jiangsu Provincial Niter and Sulfur Transportation and Sales Office representative Guan Zhi, Xu Peiruo, the Flying Flower Industry Association representatives Xie Zhongle, Gu Wenchao, Shi Shenfu, the Huang Jinrong representative Wang Riku, and the notary Song Kangfu signed a 13-article agreement, which was made in quadruplicate. Each party held one copy, and our association submitted one copy to the Ministry of Military Affairs for record. According to Article 12 of the agreement, it would be in effect forever from the date of signing. Article 13 states that the agreement cannot be changed without mutual consent. Therefore, the agreement has become a powerful contract. It cannot be changed unilaterally due to changes in personnel. The industry association has sworn not to accept the request to renegotiate, aiming to maintain the contract. We hereby inform you and hope that you will comply and allow them to proceed according to the original agreement. We hope that you will not make any changes.

Chinese Red Cross Society Sends a Large Batch of Refugees Back to Their Hometowns

Standing Committee of the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association

Passed Important Motions

The All-Zhejiang Jiaxu Drought Disaster Relief Association convened its 25th standing committee meeting yesterday afternoon. Over twenty people attended, including Shen Zhi, Yu Zhongxian, Wang Yiting, Zhuang Qing, Xu Xinliu, Chu Huizeng, Qu Wenliu, and Gu Xinyi, to discuss the spring relief measures proposed by committee member Yu Zhongxian. It was resolved that the first point would be the same as the association's original plan, and the second point would be handled as discussed. The association should send personnel to inspect and accept the completed work relief projects.

Spring Relief Plan: Yu Zhongxian's proposed spring relief plan: (1) Each county in the spring relief plan should use work as a means of relief. The main body of operation is in each county, so the association does not need to send a large number of personnel to each county as in winter relief. This time, one person can be sent to each county, and the title can be designated as the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association's work relief supervisor in a certain county, assisting officials and gentry in each county. This can save expenses and avoid the drawbacks of exclusive and isolated actions that do not conform to local public opinion. (2) Each county's work relief, whether dredging rivers or building dikes, must be examined and verified to accumulate merits. The association should elect one person from the standing committee for each county to inspect and accept the construction in each county after the construction begins, to show solemnity and prevent corruption. All expenses for the inspections will be self-provided.

Work Relief Outline: The association's work relief outline: (1) The county government should select key projects in each disaster area and design micro-projects. Anyone with the ability to work, regardless of gender, can apply. (2) The project plan should not be too large and should be directly related to farmland water conservancy, such as dredging branch rivers and small ports, raising embankment shores, and repairing ditches and weirs. Disaster victims doing work should be recruited nearby. (3) Relief rice should be distributed, calculated at one liter of rice per cubic foot, or two liters of rice per work unit. (4) Women who cannot carry heavy loads can be carried by two people, calculated as half a work unit per person per day. (5) When work stops each day, the monitor will call the roll and issue tokens. Every three days, the inspector will personally inspect and verify the tokens and exchange them for relief tickets. (6) The supervisor is appointed by the county government, and the inspector is selected and appointed by the director of the inspection department of the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association.

Li Heshang, Sentenced to Life Imprisonment, Withdraws Appeal

Voluntarily Enters Prison to Spend His Remaining Years

Li Heshang, a young man from Nanhui, 27 years old, worked as a servant for a Western family at No. 247, Lane 261, Route des Sœurs in the French Concession. His mistress, Li Yu, 25 years old, from Suzhou, worked as a cook in the same house. Li had a friend and colleague named Jin Kui, who was scheduled to get married in the first month of the lunar calendar this year. Lacking funds to make new clothes, on the afternoon of the 9th of this month, at about 4 p.m., he asked Li to hold a weapon and go to No. 3 Shanzhong Road, the Dazhonghua Coal Ball Distribution Office, to rob. They stole twelve small dollars and fled separately. Li escaped on a bicycle with a gun, heading west along Haig Road. The victim, Xu Guochang, chased after them and shouted for help. Li fled to the Zhao Zhujiao Road intersection, where he encountered a police officer No. 4, who heard the alarm and helped chase them to the Route des Sœurs intersection. Another police officer, No. 192, heard the alarm and rushed to intercept them. Li shot at the officer, killing No. 192. At the same time, Li was shot and wounded in the right leg by police officer No. 434, who returned fire. Li fled back to his employer's house and told his employer that he had been chased by the police and injured by stray bullets on the road. He asked his employer to send him to the hospital for treatment. His employer reported to the French police by phone, and Detective Zhou Buguang and others rushed to arrest Li, seizing a pistol, a bicycle, and a coat with bullet holes. Li's mistress, Yu, and his accomplice, Sun Linwen, were also arrested for helping to hide the gun and destroy evidence. They were sent to the First Special Court for prosecution on charges of robbery and murder. After the trial by Judge Zhang Chaozuo, Li Heshang was sentenced to nine years of imprisonment for carrying a weapon and committing robbery in a gang, two years of imprisonment for possessing military firearms, and life imprisonment for attempting to escape punishment by committing murder, with deprivation of civil rights for life. The life imprisonment was to be enforced. Li Yu and Sun Linwen were each sentenced to four months of imprisonment for helping to destroy evidence, with a three-year suspended sentence. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Li Heshang was dissatisfied with the verdict and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, hoping to reduce his sentence. Based on the appeal, the High Court opened a preliminary investigation court yesterday morning, presided over by Judge Xiong Ping, and ordered the police to bring the prisoner Li to the court for questioning from the detention center. Li had learned the pros and cons of the case in the detention center and feared that the appeal would result in a heavier sentence. Therefore, after the judge questioned him about his name, age, place of residence, and occupation, and asked him about his reasons for appealing against the original judgment, Li suddenly requested to withdraw his appeal and expressed his willingness to be sent to prison immediately to spend his remaining years. The court approved the request and ordered him to sign the request record. The judge ordered the bailiffs to take Li down and temporarily return him to custody, pending execution of the sentence.

Cao Xu, an old woman from Yangzhou residing at No. 430 Avenue Edward VII in the Public Concession, is 50 years old and has a daughter named Yuying, 15 years old, of average appearance. Examination Results: Yao Jinping Is Still a Virgin

Truth Revealed About the Question of a Woman Turning into a Man

Anxious to See Her Father, Fearing Many Inconveniences of a Long Journey

...General Li Du Promises to Help Her Return to Tianjin for School and Provide Living Expenses for Many Years...

Since the discovery of the case of Tianjin woman Yao Jinping turning into a man, not only has the whole country been in an uproar, but even foreigners in China, such as Mr. Fei Bai, the police superintendent of the French Concession, have been eager to see Yao in person. In particular, it has aroused deep concern among the medical community, all of whom hope to conduct an on-site examination to clarify the truth. Therefore, at the suggestion of General Li Du, he contacted Yan Fuqing, the president of the National Shanghai Medical College (formerly the Red Cross) at 363 Haige Road, by telephone three nights ago. Mr. Yan also believed that this unprecedented physiological change was of real research value to medicine, so he expressed his welcome. Thus, at about 4:00 p.m. the day before yesterday (the 19th), General Li himself, accompanied by his secretary Zheng Yucun, took Yao Jinping and her grandfather Qing Bingri in his own car from Li's residence in Jing'an Villa directly to the medical college. President Yan, to be cautious, specially summoned Dr. Gao Rimei, director of the Department of Urology and Reproductive Medicine, and Dr. Wang Yihui, director of the Department of Obstetrics, to be responsible for a precise examination to determine the truth. However, because the examination was complicated and would require at least two days in the hospital to complete, her grandfather accompanied her to the hospital and a special first-class room, No. 29 on the second floor, was set up. Details have been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday was the second day of Yao's admission to the hospital, but something unexpected happened. Yesterday afternoon, a reporter happened to visit a friend at a certain place, and Mr. Hu, a well-known insurance professional, was present. When he saw the reporter, he smiled and said, "Do you know the results of Yao Jinping's examination today?" The reporter replied, "Not yet." Mr. Hu continued (the following is all Mr. Hu's words): "This morning (that is, yesterday), I went to the Red Cross on Haige Road to visit a sick friend. When I arrived, it was already about 11:00 a.m. After talking with my friend for about ten minutes, I suddenly heard people whispering outside the room. Listening carefully, they were talking about Yao's examination. So I inquired carefully. According to a nurse, 'Just now, our doctor ordered Yao to take off her lower trousers to inspect her, but Yao refused. Although the doctor repeatedly persuaded her gently, Yao still refused. At this time, the doctors discussed it again in secret and then used a kind of irresistible drug to make Yao fall asleep on the bed and accept the examination. It turned out that Yao was a complete woman. The transformation was purely fabricated.'" Hearing this, the reporter walked to the door of Room 29 and peeked inside. He saw a person on the bed, seemingly sleeping soundly and not yet awake, and an old man sitting beside her, presumably Yao's grandfather. After hearing this, the reporter drove to the hospital at 9:00 p.m. to inquire, but the staff in the hospital were tight-lipped, only saying that Yao Jinping and her grandfather had indeed been sent back to Li's residence in Jing'an Villa by car from the hospital at about 5:00 p.m. this afternoon (yesterday) and handed over to General Li Du.

In order to be cautious, this newspaper telephoned General Li Du late at night. General Li told the truth (the following are all General Li's words): "In order to clarify the truth about Yao Jinping's transformation from a woman to a man, I specially obtained the consent of President Yan Fuqing of the National Shanghai Medical College and personally sent Yao and her grandfather to the hospital yesterday (that is, the day before yesterday). President Yan attached great importance to this matter and specially invited six doctors (two Westerners and four Chinese) to conduct a joint examination at about 9:00 a.m. today (yesterday). However, Yao refused from beginning to end. Finally, the doctor used anesthetic to put Yao to sleep. The examination showed that she was completely female. After the doctor obtained the results, he telephoned me at about 11:00 a.m. I rushed over and questioned Yao about why she did this. Yao immediately cried and told General Li that she was anxious to go to Xinjiang to find her father, but feared that there would be many inconveniences for a woman on a long journey, so she had no choice but to do this, and asked General Li to forgive her." General Li felt sorry for her and immediately took her back to his residence, asking her grandfather how much household living expenses he needed each year. Yao's grandfather replied that 300 yuan was enough. General Li immediately generously promised to subsidize 300 yuan each year and instructed Yao Jinping not to go to Xinjiang, but to return to Tianjin to go to school, and that he would continue to subsidize all her tuition fees. As for the whereabouts of her father in Xinjiang, he also promised to try to investigate.

Tongchang Car Company Uses Photos for Advertising Miss Lu Ping Sues Zhu Tongsheng

Spreading Images Related to Her Reputation

Demanding Compensation for Damages and Destruction of Publications

Lu Ping, a 23-year-old woman from Wuxi and an employee in the cosmetics department of the Xielong Trading Company at 459 North Henan Road, has received considerable education. Recently, she discovered that the Tongchang Car Company at the intersection of Yunnan Road and Nanjing Road had published her portrait in various daily newspapers and magazines, accompanied by a car rental advertisement, without her consent. Therefore, she believes that this constitutes an act of spreading obscene images and harming her reputation. She has hired lawyer Zhang Ding to file a criminal self-accusation with the First Special Court against Zhu Tongsheng, the owner of Tongchang Car Company, and Mao Keming, the director of the advertising department. The main points of her accusation are as follows: The self-accuser is an employee of Xielong Trading Company and has little social interaction. Recently, someone told her that her portrait had been found in various daily newspapers, books, pamphlets, and printed materials, in large numbers. She then searched for and identified many of them, confirming that they were indeed made by Zhu Tongsheng, the owner of Tongchang Car Company. As a woman, the self-accuser is neither an important person nor a high-ranking official, and the circulation of her portrait will not inspire respect, but will only demean her personality, make her vulnerable to frivolousness, and cause misunderstandings, which is related to her reputation. Therefore, she asked a lawyer to send a letter notifying them to immediately stop printing any unprinted daily newspapers, recall and cancel those that had already been issued, and publish an apology in the newspaper. However, the defendants refused and claimed that Mao Keming had obtained her consent to take the photos beforehand. Although Mao is a friend of the self-accuser's husband and occasionally went out for a stroll and took photos in Zhaofeng Garden, he did not explain that they would be used for Tongchang advertisements. Therefore, the defendants' use of the self-accuser's image to spread it to the public constitutes a crime under Article 325, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. In addition to compensation for damages, she reserves the right to take further action and demands that the defendants be found guilty, that the printed images be destroyed, that no further publications be made in various books and newspapers, and that the judgment be published in the newspaper at the defendants' expense according to law. Yesterday afternoon, judge Zhan Liangce presided over the trial in the Second Criminal Court. Mao Keming failed to appear after being summoned, while Zhu Tongsheng appeared in court with his lawyer Jiang Yiping. The self-accuser Lu Ping stated the previous circumstances of her complaint and stated that Mao Kepeng, a friend of her husband, invited her by telephone to take photos in Zhaofeng Garden and other places twice between July and August last year. Each time, there was a rented car beside her. At that time, she thought they were just ordinary game photos and did not pay attention. She did not know that Mao had published the photos in various newspapers and magazines as advertisements, which was a real harm to her reputation. She asked to be investigated and presented the newspapers and "Life Quick View," as well as the Rongji Da Wuhai commemorative special edition, to the court through her lawyer Zhang Ding. Zhu Tongsheng confessed that Mao Keming was previously the advertising director in my car company and has now resigned. When these photos were taken, I was not in Shanghai. Afterwards, when I read the newspaper, I asked Mao, and Mao said that the photos were published with the consent of Ms. Lu herself. Then, lawyer Jiang Yiping stood up and presented various pieces of evidence, saying that the self-accuser had taken photos with Mao Keming a total of five times, each time with a rented car beside her, sitting and standing in different positions, which was obviously with her consent. Now, because Mao's business was closed, the self-accuser came to court to file a lawsuit, and there are other relationships involved. There are witnesses who can prove it. Then, witnesses Li Afu and Zhao Asan filed a case and confessed that they were Tongchang's car drivers and proved that Mao Keming had repeatedly taken Ms. Lu to the racecourse road and Zhaofeng Garden by chartered car or motorcycle on August 31, September 2, and September 5 to take photos, all of which were voluntary, but they did not know what they were for. Judge Zhan reviewed the confession and, since Mao had not arrived, ordered the case to be adjourned until the 27th afternoon to summon Mao Keming to the court for further questioning.

Mediation Fails

Court Orders Sentence to Be Pronounced on a Scheduled Date

She only received five thousand taels of silver. In addition, as far as she knew, the defendant still held 30,000 yuan of Pacific Bank stock, as well as a large plot of land on Baohua Mountain in Nanjing. Later, the lawyers for the plaintiff and defendant debated each other to the end. Judge Zhang kindly persuaded both parties to reconcile, but it took a long time and did not work. He then ordered them to withdraw and wait for a scheduled sentence.

Habitual Thief Wants to Get Rich, Steals Airline Tickets and Flees

Mao Chengli's Greed Is Aroused

Yu Qingfeng's Partner Chases

Mao Chengli, 29 years old, from Ningbo, used to be a dock worker. Now, due to prolonged unemployment and economic hardship, he has no choice but to go out at night and sneak into shops and households to steal property to make a living. Mao heard people say that the aviation lottery tickets sold in the city's cigarette shops cost ten yuan each, and only cost one dollar per strip, but if you won the first prize, you could get a huge bonus of 500,000 yuan. The idea of getting rich arose spontaneously. Afterwards, Mao became a gold digger, thinking about buying lottery tickets day and night, but he suffered from not having money and lacking capital. At 5:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, Mao happened to pass by the entrance of Yu Qingfeng Cigarette Shop at No. 1, Dongjiadu, Nanshi. He suddenly saw that the counter of the shop was covered with aviation lottery tickets. The huge red characters of 500,000 yuan for the monthly first prize were hanging high on the wall. Mao paid attention to him there for a long time, and his eyes were dazzled by him. For a while, his mind was distracted. He saw that every lottery ticket could get 50,000 yuan, but he had no choice but to reach into his bag, and his pocket was empty. He regretted that he had more than enough heart but not enough strength. Before long, Mao suddenly had an idea, made his old trick, took advantage of the shop assistant's carelessness, reached into the cabinet, stole twelve aviation lottery tickets, and immediately turned around and ran away. He was seen by the shop assistant Huang Yongkang, who quickly took a step and chased him to the vicinity of Gongyi Wharf, where he was intercepted by Qiang Yuhua, the eleventh post guard, and searched for the original stolen goods. He was taken to the Dongjiadu Police Station under the jurisdiction of the station director, and Mao Chengli confessed that the reason I stole lottery tickets was nothing more than wanting to get rich. If I won the first prize, I would immediately become a rich man, and I could have cars and foreign houses as I wanted, and I could use my concubines and slaves as I wanted, and I would no longer have to be a thief and taste the wind, frost, rain and snow, and eat people's fists. Because the matter involved a theft case, he was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the bureau for investigation.

Yan Zirong Plans Viciously One Woman Can't Be Married to Two

Both Crimes Are Sent to the Court for Questioning

Yan Zirong, 50 years old, from Yangzhou, nicknamed "Old Candle," lives in a grass shed in Chongdeli, Renji Road, Pudong, and works as a dock worker. More than ten years ago, he had an affair with a woman. At that time, the woman brought a daughter named Guizhen, who has been living with her ever since. Now Guizhen is 20 years old. At the beginning of last year, she fell in love with Chen Yongfu's son Dexi, a fellow villager who opened a barber shop at No. 6 in the same neighborhood. At the beginning of last month, Guizhen suddenly disappeared, so Yan used his father's name to twist Dexi to the Pudong Public Security Bureau on the ninth of last month, accusing him of enticing his daughter, and Wang Xiuying, a woman from the same village, was brought to the case to prove that Guizhen was indeed hidden by Dexi. Later, the bureau sent both parties to the local court. After investigation, the court sentenced Dexi to six months in prison to serve as a warning, because the witness testimony was accurate. Dexi's father Yongfu felt uneasy because his son was imprisoned and suffered injustice. He spent money to hire two old women to search for Guizhen's whereabouts in various places every day, hoping that the truth would come out. But it was coincidental that the two old women recently passed through the Zhuangyuan area of ​​Hongkou and suddenly saw Guizhen performing in a circus troupe set up on the wasteland. They immediately returned to Pudong to report the news. Yongfu twisted Guizhen and Wang Sun, the female head of the circus troupe, to the relevant police station for investigation. At that time, Sun produced a marriage certificate, proving that Guizhen was sold to her son as his wife by her biological father Guo Guoyun, and Yu Chunxiang and Wang Guobao were matchmakers. It was agreed that the betrothal gift was 120 yuan, and 40 yuan had been paid. However, Wang turned the money over to Guizhen's stepfather Yan Zirong to collect it. Soon, the police station ruled that the case was a marital dispute and ordered that it not be dealt with. At this point, Yongfu realized that Yan had first conspired with Guizhen's former father to sell her at a price, and then falsely accused his son of trying to defraud him of his losses. So, he returned to Pudong and found Yan in a small teahouse on Dongchang Road at 10:00 a.m. yesterday. He first covered his head with a purse and reported to the police, and then took him to the Pudong Sub-bureau. During the pre-trial by the bureau chief, Yongfu stated that he had been framed by Yan, and discovered the behind-the-scenes events. He requested an investigation. According to Yan's confession, Guizhen was still enticed by the plaintiff's son. The bureau chief then sent the police to Hongkou to summon Wang Sun and Guizhen from the circus troupe together. According to Guizhen's confession, she was sold by her biological father and was not hidden by the plaintiff's son, and Sun confessed that the former father of Guizhen and the defendant had agreed to sell Guizhen to my son as his wife. The betrothal gift of 40 yuan was also received by the defendant. At this point, Director Zhang realized that Yan had planned viciously, framed good people, and made the plaintiff's son go to jail innocently. He was an extremely cunning and stubborn person. Just as he was about to send the case for investigation, the local court sent a subpoena, chasing the defendant Yan Zirong to ask questions. The reason was that a certain person named Jia from Taizhou accused Yan of first betrothing his daughter Guizhen to his son, and now he married Guizhen to the son of the circus owner. Please investigate the situation. Director Zhang believed that Yan had committed two crimes, one woman marrying two men, and he issued both crimes and ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the local court for joint investigation.

Dancing Girl Li Xiuying Accuses University Student Pan Xunzhi; After Yesterday's Debate, Verdict Set for the 23rd

Pan Xunzhi from Anhui, a graduate of Fudan University, 26 years old, already married with children, residing at No. 18, Yongfu South Lane, Donghan Bi Li Road, was sued in the First Special District Court by Li Xiuying from Ningbo (17 years old), a dancing girl at the Dadong Dance Hall, along with her mother Li Zhang, engaging lawyers Huang Xiu Bo and Huang Xiu Qi for charges of luring, restricting freedom, and causing injury under Articles 257, 318, and 293 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zeshu of the First Special Court conducted a trial in the First Criminal Division. Both parties appeared in court as summoned. Li Xiuying testified that she works as a dancing girl at the Dadong Dance Hall and also performs tea dances at the Xinhua Dance Hall. She met the defendant, Pan Xunzhi, through dancing about a year ago. On January 6th of this year, the defendant invited her out, and after dancing at the Yangzi Hotel dance hall, she was taken to room 717 upstairs and raped. Because she resisted at the time, the defendant wrote her a note promising to marry her, or else give her 4,000 yuan for living expenses. Later, she was raped again in room 433 of the Shangdu Hotel. Her mother was unaware of this. On the 12th of this month, she was taken to the home of a Mr. Wang on Xiamen Road, and forced to sign a note stating she was willing to marry the defendant, or else be fined 4,000 yuan. Due to the use of force, she had no choice but to comply. That evening, the defendant forbade her from dancing with other customers. She called her mother, but the defendant injured her mother's breasts, eyes, and other parts of her body, hence the lawsuit. Li Zhang also submitted evidence of the assault. Pan Xunzhi stated in his defense that his relationship with Li Xiuying began before January 6th, at rooms 812 or 814 of the Yangzi Hotel, not 717. The note was written after the relationship began, and they stayed together numerous times, which he cannot recall. The note written by Li Xiuying was of her own free will, without coercion. He already had a wife, which Li knew and had even met. His current residence at No. 29 Xiamen Road was rented by Li, and the note she gave him stated that everything she owned belonged to Pan Xunzhi, and if she remarried or behaved improperly, she would compensate Pan with 4,000 yuan. The dispute on March 12th arose because a dance customer did not give Li Xiuying a dance ticket after dancing with her. He questioned her why she didn't ask the customer for it, and her answer was vague. He questioned her again, and she called her mother, who brought over twenty gangsters who severely beat him, causing injuries. In self-defense, he fought back. He then reported the incident, and they were both taken to the Laozha Police Station, where it was confirmed that injuries were present. The plaintiff's testimony was mostly fabricated. Judge Wu, after reviewing the testimonies and considering the facts clear, ordered the debate to begin and announced that the verdict would be delivered on the morning of the 23rd. Pan was released on 200 yuan bail.

Mutual Accusations of Adultery: Longtime Couple Suddenly Become Bitter Enemies; Wife Catches Husband in Adultery, Takes Him to the Police Station for Reprimand, Then Released; Husband Catches Wife in Adultery, Sends Her to Court, Court Orders Acquittal

Ma Zhishui from Ningbo, 40 years old, engaged in the business of clocks, watches, and phonographs, married Mao, also from Ningbo, 39 years old, for over twenty years. Their relationship was generally good, with one son and one daughter, both grown and married. Three years ago, Ma and Mao suddenly had disagreements, became suspicious of each other, and went to extremes, eventually leading to litigation. Ma filed a lawsuit in court, seeking a divorce from Mao. The court ruled against Ma. Since then, Ma and Mao were husband and wife in name only, but actually lived separately. Ma paid 30 yuan per month for living expenses, and Mao lived alone at No. 10, Lane 448, Tianjin Road. However, Ma initially paid the living expenses, but after two months, he claimed he could not afford it and stopped paying. Mao filed a lawsuit in court, requesting the court to order her husband to fulfill the contract. After repeated trials, the case went on for years, until the Supreme Court finally concluded the matter. From then on, their feelings became increasingly worse, and the loving couple became bitter enemies. Both sides schemed and plotted to retaliate. On the 3rd of last month, Mao discovered that her husband, Ma Zhishui, was having an affair with a woman and went to catch them in the act, but was reprimanded and dismissed after taking them to the police station. Then, on the evening of the night before last, around 11 PM, Ma also discovered that his wife was having an affair with Xu Wenhan from Shaoxing (Xu is 48 years old and the eldest son of Xu Qianlin, the general manager of the Jiangwan Model Factory) at her residence on Tianjin Road. Ma led his younger brother Ma Xiangyuan, and shop employees Zhu Gongkuan and Chen A'hai to catch them in the act. Upon entering the room, they found Mao and Xu together. They called Chinese Constable No. 798, who arrested Mao and Xu and took them to the Laozha Police Station, where they were detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were charged with adultery under Article 256 of the Criminal Code, with the woman being a married woman. Zhang Shizhu, the police station's lawyer, stated the case, saying that both defendants denied having committed adultery in the police station, requesting further investigation. Ma Zhishui stated that Mao was his wife, and they had been separated for many years. He had known about Mao's improper behavior and affair with Xu for two years, but lacking evidence, he secretly investigated until last night when he confirmed Xu had entered his wife's residence again for adultery. He led his brother and others to catch them. They found the door locked and broke in, finding the two lying in bed together. Xu was naked from the waist down, while Mao had already put on her clothes. He immediately called the Chinese constable to have Xu put on his pants and taken to the police station. He requested severe punishment and compensation for losses. Chinese Constable No. 798 and witnesses Ma Xiangyuan and others also submitted evidence. Mao stated that after separating from her husband Ma Zhishui, she opened the Dalu Phonograph Company on Tianjin Road and rented the remaining rooms to Xu Wenhan, who opened the Deda Phonograph Company. Last night, she summoned Xu to settle accounts, but her husband gathered over a dozen people and assaulted them without explanation, forcibly stripping Xu's pants, accusing them of adultery, and taking them to the police station. She claimed she did not commit adultery and that her husband was retaliating for her previous attempt to catch him in adultery. Xu Wenhan also denied adultery. He Ma, 20 years old, the daughter of Ma and Mao, testified that she lived with her mother in the pavilion room, while her mother lived in the front building. After her mother separated from her father, they opened the Dalu Phonograph Company due to financial difficulties and sought help from Xu Qianlin, a comprador at the Shengli Phonograph Company, who sent his eldest son Xu Wenhan to help with the business, but there was no misconduct. Last night, her father came, claiming to be catching adultery and locking her room door. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the police station stated that Ma Zhishui had known about this matter two years ago. According to Article 218 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the statute of limitations has expired. Judge Ye ruled that both defendants should be acquitted, and the related civil suit should be transferred to the Civil Court for trial.

Reason for Ping Zhimen's Suicide

Ping Zhimen, a local real estate broker, had been operating in Shanghai for years. On the 11th of this month, he was found in the bathroom of the International Recreation Club on Jing'an Temple Road with his left artery severed by a razor. The case was investigated at the police station by Mr. Haines of the U.S. Consulate a few days ago. First, the deceased's son testified that his father had recently shown signs of suicide. At the beginning of this month, when he went to bed, his mother noticed that his expression was different, so she and her children searched him and found a pistol in his pocket. Spring and Autumn

Snippets

— (Sha Yongcai) (Yan Xinquan)

When President Zhang Boling of Nankai University and his wife, Wang Shuzhen, held a celebration for their 40th wedding anniversary in Nankai Auditorium, he said in his speech: "Wives often hope that their husbands will get rich, but they don't know that the first person their husbands will dislike when they get rich is you." "In the responsibility for a harmonious marriage, men should take 65% to 70%, and women should only take 30% to 35%." "Both sides must lower their status, be able to tolerate and yield, and not be afraid to lie, which is a good way to achieve harmony." These clever words contain profound truths. These few sentences are worth a manual on wifemanship or husbandmanship.

Tian Xu Wo Sheng recently published a statement in the newspaper regarding those who send free books and letters in seven-character sentences. Although it has a humorous meaning, we cannot regard it as humorous writing. I am now transcribing it as follows: "Chinese people should use domestic products; everyone recognizes this statement. Although I cannot force others, others cannot force me. I especially hate letters or publications that use foreign paper. I often put them on a high shelf unopened, or throw them into the fire. I have not seen the text in them. Postal registration must be correct. It is not laziness or failure to reply. It is because of this that I am letting down the kindness."

Sequel to Records of Strange Surnames

— Citizen's Words

In the March 7th issue of this publication, Mr. Wan's "Records of Strange Surnames" listed mostly names of celebrities, which naturally many people would know. However, I also know a few surnames that Mr. Wan didn't mention, which are also considered strange by the general public. As for whether they are in the Hundred Family Surnames? Because I haven't read it, I can only ignore that. I am writing them out now as a further addition to it. (Gong) This is my surname. I have wandered north and south for twenty years and rarely encountered a clan member. Four or five years ago, Gong Bingfan, who was a teacher in Jiangxi, was said to have moved from Henan to Shaanxi, and was indeed a member of the same family. Apart from that, on the opera bills in Guangzhou, you often see Gong ××, but I don't know if that's their surname. (Mu) Ten years ago, I visited a classmate at the Guanzhong Hall in Beiping. At that time, as soon as he saw me, he shouted "Old Mu, Old Mu!" "Come quickly, come quickly!" "Now I've found you a Gong." After a while, this Mr. Mu came in and laughed heartily, saying, "It's very interesting. Once I went to the post office to mail a letter, and there were many people waiting for registration. Among them, a young man kept smiling at me. I was completely baffled. Later, when I saw his envelope, I suddenly understood. It turned out he wrote 'Father' sealed, while I wrote 'Mother' sealed. That's when I realized that Father is also a surname." (Yun) Is the surname of my grandmother's family. (Suo) Cun De is my cousin. He served as the patrol inspector of Linggu in Shaanxi during the late Qing Dynasty. (Ju) Zhang Baomin was a general under Guo Jian of Shaanxi in the 1920s. People called him Commander Dog. (Yan) Zhilan was a division commander under Fan Zhongxiu. (Gong) Fu Kui (Ji) and Xifeng were both commanders during the Jingguo Army era in Shaanxi. Both were from Shanxi. (Tie) When I was in Xi'an, there was a noodle shop owner surnamed Tie. I heard he was a Muslim. (Hua) Lianshi was a famous gentleman from Gongxian County, Henan. (Shan) Shuibin is a merchant from Henan. Now living in Dongxin Jujushun Gong. Aren't the others, like (Diao) Banhua, who co-starred in "Han Jiang Luo Yan" with Lianhua and Chen Yan; lawyer (Li) Aokui; shot put athlete (Yi) Ming, all rarely seen surnames?

New News from the Lake

— Master of Shi Garden

Time passes like a stream, and on West Lake, peach blossoms are just blooming, and new willows are already green. The mountain is like a painting, gradually entering its best scenery. The six bridges and three temples are once again a different kind of beauty. It is only a matter of time before the bees and butterflies come and go like a tide.

The tour boats on the lake have recently seen gradual progress. In the past, the antique-style seats with copper railings have all been replaced since last year with two-seater or three-seater armchairs, with kapok cushions covered with white ruffled covers. Sitting comfortably on them, either leaning forward or back, leisurely in the middle of the stream, already feels more comfortable than usual. This spring there is even further improvement, with quite a proactive arrangement of sofa-style seats, four seats per boat, covered with cream-colored chair covers. In recent days, one or two have already been seen appearing on the lakefront. It is predicted that this will be a uniform era of improvement. Although it is close to Europeanization, people sitting on them ultimately find their minds and spirits more comfortable.

After the reconstruction of Baochu Pagoda, the Six Harmonies Pagoda will also be demolished and rebuilt. The drawings have been completed by architect Tada, and the original shape will not be changed slightly. A garden will also be arranged around the pagoda's base so that after visiting the pagoda, people can relax their feet a bit more. This plan is truly well conceived. I heard that the project will still be led by the municipal government, and funds have been helped by celebrities from all walks of life. Before long, it will be transformed, and next spring, it may be able to meet us with a new appearance, which is not necessarily known. Recently, Hangzhou established a Scenic Spot Guide Bureau within the Construction Department. In the future, those who come to this place can go to the bureau to request the dispatch of a knowledgeable guide, who will leisurely travel around, so as not to be like blowing a flute without holes, or eating "cucumbers" to the point of exhaustion. It is also heard that the bureau is currently recruiting and examining tour guides, and is actively engaged in training, in order to meet the needs.

Among the six parks on the lakefront, there was previously the "Chen Yingshi Memorial Tower," and the "Memorial Tower for the Martyrs of the Northern Expedition." Recently, the "Memorial Tower for the Martyrs of the 88th Division in the Battle of Shanghai" has been completed, standing tall on the lakefront, extremely majestic. It is enough to give a dose of stimulants to the West Lake tourists who are infatuated with the gentle land.

A Mystery of Life

— Zi Wei

I was casually talking with a friend, and we got on the topic of so-and-so's situation. In less than a year, he had been promoted three levels in a row. The treatment in this organization cannot be said to be unkind. However, so-and-so, in the same position and the same job, is still the same as before. Not only is there no hope of promotion, but his own job is also a bit shaky.

According to my friend, Mr. B's knowledge is much more profound than Mr. A's. He is also very diligent in his official duties, but he has a somewhat "you are you, I am I" temperament, so his director and he don't get along very well. As for Mr. A, he relies on his talent and is arrogant, looking down on everything, but he is submissive to his immediate superior, with pleasing expressions and laughter. When casually chatting with others, he must argue for the director's virtue and talent at every mention of their director, placing him high above everyone else. Although people scoff at it, Mr. A acts as if nothing happened, with a general attitude of "let people laugh and scold."

As the end of the year approached, the authorities inquired of the director about the performance appraisal, and the director strongly defended Mr. A, saying that Mr. A was prudent in public matters, quick in his work, and a leader among his peers. Mr. B was slow and procrastinating, and not worth mentioning. The authorities nodded.

Days later, the public announcement was made, and Mr. A was indeed honored with a key position, while Mr. B was severely reprimanded and retained on probation.

Afterwards, my friend discussed this matter with his old man, who greatly praised Mr. A's skill in dealing with the world. My friend disagreed, saying, "Based on the director's words alone, the success or failure is immediately apparent. However, the authorities have not carefully examined it even once." The old man said, "You are truly a fool. In today's world, you still want to use your true skills as a way to earn a living? No wonder you will die old under the window, not being used by the world." My friend still argued strongly, his anger still not subsided, so he told me about it, wanting a fair judgment. I simply said, "Mr. A certainly has the art of ascending to greatness, and the old man is experienced in the ways of the world. Speaking of this kind of mystery of life, how can you and I possibly break it?"

News about Distinguished Ladies’ Paintings: This year's Women's Painting and Calligraphy Exhibition is being actively prepared. Ms. Chen Xiaocui is invited to be the chief editor of the catalogue, the contents of which will include selected works of calligraphy, painting, poetry, lyrics and prose by women. In addition to soliciting works from members of this association, contributions from the female community are welcome. The deadline is March 13th. Please send submissions to No. 59, Anlefang, Jing'an Temple, Shanghai.

Records of Lingering Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Because the facilities provided by the Empress Dowager for silkworm raising were so elaborate, the girls raising the silkworms were also extra careful, but every day, several tens of silkworms – about two or three per thousand – inevitably died due to various reasons. But even if we found dead silkworms, we were absolutely not allowed to say "a silkworm died," and could only silently pick it out. Not only that, but there were many more superstitious customs in silkworm raising! No one was allowed to point at a certain silkworm and say "not good," or "ugly," or other bad words; if they said so, then the silk spun by these silkworms later would inevitably also be "not good" or "ugly." And these girls who specialized in raising silkworms each wore a very wide ribbon tied on their heads, so that their hair would not be scattered at all, supposedly as a model for the silkworms to see; after they saw it, the silk they spun would also not be scattered at all. These girls also wore another brightly colored belt tied around their waists, cinching their waists very tightly, supposedly also as a model for the silkworms to see; after they saw it, the cocoons they made would generally also be particularly thin in the middle and thick and round at both ends, with a very good appearance. These girls in the silkworm room not only could not say bad words, but also had to constantly say a few flattering or encouraging words to the silkworms, like educating a child, so that at the final harvest, they could obtain very fine silk.

Although the color of the silkworms themselves is generally grayish-white, the silk they spin has pure white and golden yellow colors, with golden yellow being more valuable. (273)

Odds and Ends

A Multifaceted View of Ruan Lingyu's Suicide

— Ding Ming

Shanghai is the Paris of the Orient, a paradise built on hell. Since International Women's Day on March 8th, the forum of the press has focused its explosive point on the suicide of movie star Ruan Lingyu, making it even more apparent.

When Ruan Lingyu's stinking carcass (in Buddhist terms) was placed in the International Funeral Home, putting on a final show of "new woman" radiance, everyone who read the newspaper focused their gaze on her body or in the newspaper: There were different opinions about the great change in people's hearts, and there were also different ways of saying that it greatly changed people's hearts. We might as well analyze it and shine an X-ray on all aspects.

Placed in the stubborn mindset of people in a capitalist feudal society, they will definitely shake their heads and wag their tails, scolding her fiercely, "A good horse doesn't wear two saddles, a good woman doesn't marry twice"; death is too good for her.

Placed in the eyes of the proletariat, they will curl their lips and snort! "Tch, weak thing!"

Placed at the corners of movie fans' mouths, they will touch their scalps, tears falling on their cheeks, greatly saddened by the future of the film industry; or they will beat their chests and stomp their feet, shedding tears of sympathy.

Placed in the minds of those who are deeply suffering from love, they will feel a bucket of cold water poured over their heads, sobering them up. And those in love triangles will automatically untie their loops.

Placed on the hearts of movie performers, they may sigh and weep; or they may think this is her delusion; or they may think this is no different than offering a burning bomb to the International Women's Day; there may even be those who secretly rejoice that Ruan Lingyu's death will allow them (the second person) to take her place!

Placed in front of the film circle's environment, actors will refuse to perform tragic scripts; theaters will also cater to the general public's psychology and show optimistic films.

Placed in the heart of Ruan Lingyu before her death, her spirit must have been comforting itself: her inner spirit warned her that reality was ugly and contradictory; the external villains were oppressing and attacking her, it was better to die! Dying caused everyone to laugh, get angry, shed tears, sigh, be angry, imagining countless men and women showing different expressions, as enthusiastic as watching her performances on the screen; that was truly the culmination of film art; laughing at Ai Xia's covering up, without the subtlety of her performance.

Placed in the perspective of psychologists, they must have understood her drunken state after attending a friend's banquet for seven days and nights, her mad kissing, her unrestrained dancing, her enjoyment; suddenly throwing a smoke screen at midnight, writing a suicide note as if returning to death, how heroic, how natural; it was purely a sensitive nerve action filled with emotion by a tragic actress. This posture of secretly singing when happy, and laughing wildly when crying, was also her only way of self-consolation and discharge in her lonely life.

However, I extremely approve of what a certain newspaper commentator said: I hope that those who want to die for love will change the direction of this kind of "martyrdom for litigation" or other martyrdom for love, martyrdom for righteousness... and express it in revolutionary actions in the women's movement.

— Jiang Mi

Why don't you dress up a little prettier?

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

When we arrived, we stayed in a small hotel here. Although I heard there was a Little Western Paradise, I didn't invite guests or meet friends, so I never came here. More than half a month after that Mr. Lian left, his friend sent me a postcard from Nanjing, saying that he had gone to Guangdong and advised me not to wait bitterly in Xi'an and to plan my return south as soon as possible. At that time, I received this letter, and I was both scared and angry, and cried for a long time. The hotel owner, on the other hand, was conscientious. He said, "Things have come to this point, you have to quickly think of a way. Crying randomly, can you cry out any reason?" I said, "Coming to Xi'an, I have no relatives or friends, where can I go to think of a way? Even that Mr. Lian only knew a few people in Xi'an, but they had nothing to do with him and嫌he came here." They stopped paying attention to him long ago. I am not his woman, just someone he cheated into coming here, and people will not pay attention to me even more." The hotel owner said again, "If you were indeed cheated here by him, people might forgive you. If you say you are his woman, people won't help you." I thought about it, and this was probably true, so I honestly told his friends about this matter. I also went to various hotels to look for people from the East, hoping for a chance. From that time on, I came to Little Western Paradise, and at that time, I fell another step down. I met a few fellow villagers in Little Western Paradise, and they didn't refuse me much, asking me to accompany them to smoke opium and play cards, often giving me a few dollars to cover my expenses. There were always new people from the East coming to the various hotels, and new fellow villagers introducing old fellow villagers, so I took advantage of this opportunity to mingle with the fellow villagers, mixing until now. Everyone calls me Miss Yang, to cover my face. Actually..." His face was pale and injured, and he couldn't say the words. (162)

Finance Under Sassoon's Fierce Suppression, the Gold Market's Rise Was Fleeting

People's Hearts Were Still Stable, with More Trading After the Lows, Resulting in a Drop of $1.30

After the gold market's sudden surge the previous morning, yesterday's market still had lingering momentum, once approaching the $80 mark. The exchange market failed to keep pace, and the rise was suppressed. The central bank wanted to block the remittance orders, and Sassoon took the opportunity to sell US dollars. The domestic market loosened, and the price fell back immediately. However, people's hearts still seemed prosperous, and the final result was a state of fluctuation. In the early morning, the overseas silver market showed a slight drop in London and stability in the US. The forward silver market also fell, but only slightly. Exchange rates rebounded, and London's raw gold rose by 3.5 pence. Reports said that the Belgian cabinet was overthrown by the opposition for supporting the gold standard, and the position of the French franc was shaken, which would affect the London gold market and indirectly affect the central bank's appetite for spot trading, causing people's hearts to darken. The over-the-counter preliminary trading opened, falling from $73.4 to just over $70. The central bank's official exchange rates were announced, with London unchanged and the US rising by 1.875. The customs gold unit rose by 3%. The standard price for tenders rose to $913.60. Major players maintained their positions at low prices, and the psychology of retail investors turned prosperous again, and the price rebounded immediately after the lows. However, the morning opening was low, and the price hovered uncertainly after the opening. Exchange rates were normal, and once fell, nearly touching the $70 mark. Buying interest revived after the lows, and gradually pulled the price up. Chinese merchants' appetite tended to be aggressive, but it was difficult to find a counterparty. Banks traded with each other, the domestic market tightened, and the rise intensified, but it did not break through the $80 mark. After the high, the supply gradually increased, and it was anticipated that the Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's (HSBC) official exchange rates would be announced, with London and the US shrinking by 0.125 each. Rice Prices Fall for Consecutive Days

—Dongyang Gang Actively Purchases Yesterday—

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of supply for each gang was still only about 20 companies (with a total of nearly 4,000 shi of goods). Among them, Su Tong's粳 [japonica rice] was even scarcer. However, both retail and wholesale sales were sluggish. Only the Yantai gang bought more than a hundred packages. Therefore, the overall market price repeatedly showed a soft tone. The rest of Su Tong's粳 depended on the small amount of goods arriving to maintain their position. The prices of other items such as Qingjiao's [green corner rice] and other thin indica rices, and the early indica rice from the Nan Gang gang, continued to fall by one "jiao". Du Yangjian [rice variety] lacked goods and had no market. Yin Yuan [silver yuan rice] was currently weak.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, more than ten boats arrived from various roads downstream. Transactions for each type of goods were sparse on the market. Spot prices for top-grade white 粳 rice were slightly higher, while mid- and low-grade goods were stable. The retail of thin indica and early indica rice was not smooth, and the price was short by nearly a "jiao". The rest also showed a soft trend. However, Bai Yuan [white yuan rice] was very tight, and although the sales of Ke Yuan [guest yuan rice] were not good, the price remained stable.

(Foreign Rice) Domestic sales were still active, and there were also dealings in this street. Therefore, the market was still relatively lively. However, the market inventory was full, and arrivals were continuous. Small and long-grain West loans were heavily stockpiled, and many firms were willing to lower prices to sell off. Therefore, yesterday it fell by three to five "fen". Other grades remained flat. Yesterday, Saigon's March re-entry goods opened at 400 tons, and the price dropped to 4 yuan and 2 jiao and a half, which was more than two "jiao" lower than the previous week. Currently, more than 8,000 bags of foreign rice and 550 bags of Ke Xian [guest xian rice] are open for sale, most of which are handled by the domestic market.

(Soybeans) Sales were slightly more active than the previous day, so the market was relatively stable. At present, the general trend is paying attention to the intensity of cake sales. It is estimated that more than 40,000 pieces of soybean cake were traded in spot and futures. The factory side purchased more than 5,000 bags of various beans in a rolling manner.

(Red Continued) Japanese sales rebounded because they saw that the selling price had fallen by more than half a yuan. Therefore, they purchased at a cheap price. Yesterday, they went to various grains for more than 2,000 bags, and the market price continued to rise by six to seven "fen".

Bran Prices Step by Step Reverting Slightly

Recently, bran exports have been in a state of long-term dormancy. Domestic transactions are not many. After foreign wheat arrives, factories have gradually more bran to sell. Although the factories are still holding on and not selling, those who return re-entry goods are more willing to lower prices to sell off. Yesterday, there were slightly more domestic sales, and the selling price has fallen to 2 yuan, 5 jiao, and 6 "fen".

Police Brigade Basketball Team Loses to Jinan University: Jinan Performs Beautifully, Winning 57 to 39. The Police Brigade, New to the Venue, Was Unfamiliar and Even Famous Players Were Below Par.

The Wuhan Police Brigade basketball team is a mixed group of athletes from the north. Key players Liu Zhenyuan and Yin Hongxiang are among them. Duan Zhuo and Wang Zhan were previously selected for the Beijing championships. Ge Ke, Wang Jianmin, Zheng Sen, and others are famous players from Central China. They all came to Shanghai to show their skills during the national team tryouts in Shanghai for the Far Eastern Games a few years ago. In terms of talent, they are all outstanding. This time, led by Song Ruhai, they came to Shanghai. Last night, they made their debut against Jinan University in a match at Shenyuan, but their performance was not up to par. They lost to Jinan 39 to 57. The team's coordination was decent, but their shooting was inaccurate, and they were unable to defend the large court adequately. The loss was entirely due to unfamiliarity. As for Jinan's victory, it was truly due to their actual skill and not a fluke.

Unfamiliar Venue

The competition was tense and exciting. Initially, Jinan missed several shots, which was quite disappointing. Later, they gradually became more familiar with the court. Han Zhenyuan and Yin Jinren's corner shots were very accurate. The Police Brigade team, being new to the venue, felt flustered and focused their defense on the middle, neglecting the sides. Jinan took advantage of this and scored repeatedly, with the score soaring. The difference reached a large gap of 23 to 3. The Police Brigade was at a disadvantage and tried hard to rally. At halftime, they were behind 13 to 25. In the second half, the Police Brigade did not improve and could only maintain the status quo without being able to win. Jinan's shooting was very accurate, and their offense and defense were excellent. The Police Brigade seemed inferior. Liu Zhenyuan had regressed a lot, while Yin Hongxiang was as steady as ever.

At a Loss

After the start, Jinan's Han Zhenyuan opened the scoring with a free throw. Then, he missed a sure shot under the basket, which was a pity. Xu Heng added points with a free throw, but the score remained close. The Police Brigade's Ge Ke received a clever pass from Liu Zhenyuan under the basket and jumped up to score, which boosted the morale of the spectators. Cai Yanxiong also added two points for Jinan. At this time, the Police Brigade's Wang Jianmin had already committed three fouls and was replaced by the famous player Yin Hongxiang. Unexpectedly, the Police Brigade did not improve. Liu Zhenyuan was frustrated, and Ge Ke was closely guarded by Xu Heng, making it impossible to score. Jinan's left and right flanks moved quickly, and their dribbling skills were excellent. Han Zhenyuan and Yin Guiren repeatedly scored side shots, gaining great momentum. The Police Brigade could not penetrate deep into the opposing side due to tight defense. Their coordination seemed lacking, and they made no progress, resulting in a score of 23 to 3. Jinan took a commanding lead.

A Glimmer of Hope

The Police Brigade replaced Duan Zhuo with Zheng Sen. Ge Ke scored their second basket, making it 23 to 5. Jinan softened slightly. The bald-headed Zheng Sen suddenly dribbled and scored two baskets, both successful. Wang Zhan also scored one basket, and Zheng Sen added two more points, making it 25 to 13. They seemed to be gaining momentum. However, halftime arrived, and the game resumed with even more intensity. The Police Brigade tried hard to break the deadlock, while Jinan did not relax at all. Both sides scored, and the situation was balanced at 37 to 23. The Police Brigade was still 12 points behind, but then Jinan's performance improved again, and the athletes from Central China fell into disarray.

Disparate Situation

Jinan relied on accurate shooting from all their players, and their score gradually increased. The Police Brigade only managed to score one basket through Yin Hongxiang, making the score 45 to 15, a difference of 20 points. Liu Zhenyuan, who had accomplished nothing, finally opened his scoring record. From then on, the score difference remained between 18 and 20 points. Xu Heng scored a basket, making it 57 to 35. Jinan had victory within their grasp. Han and Cai were successively substituted, entering the reserves. The Police Brigade struggled desperately, and Duan Zhuo scored two consecutive baskets, resulting in a final score of 57 to 39. The referees were Zhou Jia and Zhai Hongren. Tomorrow night, the Police Brigade will play against Donghua University.

Xu Chengji Performance

Defeats Xu Weipei in Hong Kong

Hong Kong, 20th. Xu Chengji, our country's representative for the Davis Cup, played an exhibition match with Xu Weipei, the Hong Kong singles tennis champion, at 4:30 AM on the 20th. Xu won in straight sets, defeating Xu significantly.

Far Eastern Games Tryout 10,000-Meter Champion, Sun Che's Coffin Transported to Jin

Sun Che, a soldier of the Zhengtai Railway Protection Army in Shanxi, the 10,000-meter champion in the tryouts for last year's Far Eastern Games, was about to go to the Philippines to win glory for the country. Unfortunately, he contracted pneumonia and liver disease. He was treated at the Red Cross Hospital but unexpectedly passed away at midnight on May 24th. The whole country mourned. The Xie Jin Association took care of the funeral arrangements, and the coffin was kept at the Qilu Hall. It has been almost a year. Now, the regimental commander of his army's 1st regiment has sent the regiment's adjutant, Xie Qifeng, to Shanghai to contact the Xie Jin Association about taking the coffin back to Jin. The association sent someone to contact the China Travel Service to handle the arrangements, which have been completed. The transport is scheduled to begin today, via train to Beijing, then transferred to PingSui, and finally to Gaotang County, Shanxi, his hometown, for burial. Sun was 30 years old, from Gaotang County, Shanxi. He served in the army for five battles and was the deputy squad leader of the Zhengtai Railway Protection Army. He was of moderate height, amiable, and won the 10,000-meter championship at the previous North China Games in 36 minutes and 4 seconds. In last year's North China tryouts, he broke the national record with 34 minutes and seconds. At the national tryouts in Shanghai, he was selected as the representative for the Far Eastern Games with a time of 34 minutes and 4 seconds, setting a new national record. Such a genius, unfortunately, did not live long, which is deeply regrettable.

East Asia Women's Basketball and Track and Field Team Tour South, Warmly Welcomed by Overseas Chinese

Track and Field Chen Shuqing Sets New 100-Meter Record, Basketball Team Wins Almost Every Game with Superb Skill, Team Returns North with Great Reputation, Expected to Arrive in Shanghai on the 26th

(Singapore Correspondence) Shanghai East Asia Sports Academy, to promote women's sports and connect with overseas Chinese, responded to the invitation of the Singapore Chinese Basketball Association and organized a southern tour team. The team, including Principal Chen Mengyu, leader Li Huaifen, captain Qian Hangsu, vice-captain Wang Huachang, and players Xue Piwei, Chen Shuqing, Chen Liqing, Qin Chiming, Xu Yuan, Pan Jingxian, and Wang Yuying, a total of twelve people, arrived in Singapore on a French postal ship from Saigon on February 5th. They were warmly welcomed by overseas Chinese and performed basketball and track and field events, achieving excellent results. They also went to Malaysia and other places for competitions, with unprecedented enthusiasm. Details are as follows:

Singapore Overseas Chinese Warmly Welcome

Since receiving the news of the East Asia Southern Tour Team's arrival in Singapore, the Singapore sports community has been actively welcoming them. Those who came to welcome included Lin Lingmin, chairman of the Singapore Chinese Basketball and Volleyball Association, Qiu Weijin, secretary-general, committee members Zheng Jieyang and Xi Yandao, the Chongzheng Alumni Association, the Amateur Sports Association, Overseas Chinese High School, Aitong Alumni Association, Weiyang Sports Association, Gongshang Alumni Association, Nanyang Girls' High School, Singapore Girls' High School, Chinese Sports Association, Chongwu Sports Association, and the school's alumni in Singapore, numbering in the hundreds. When the ship arrived, cheers erupted. Principal Chen shook hands with each welcomer. Compatriots from the motherland meeting in a foreign land experienced a joy that words cannot describe.

Sanjiang Guild Hall Hosts Tea Party

The Sanjiang Guild Hall, to connect with fellow villagers, held a tea party at its Dongling Gabizhi Road clubhouse at 10 AM on the 10th to express their welcome. The event began with a speech by Shi Shaozeng, the Chinese Consul General in Singapore, who said that the East Asia team's outstanding performances would give overseas Chinese a good understanding of the new national education in the motherland and provide them with a principle to emulate. He added that women's sports in the South Seas were generally backward and expressed hope that the East Asia team's visit would raise awareness among women in Singapore. Principal Chen of East Asia then gave a speech, reporting the purpose of the trip. Finally, Qian Hangsu thanked the audience in fluent Mandarin. The event ended around 12 PM. In addition, there were countless invitations to banquets, keeping them very busy.

Establishing a Special Committee for Competition Liaison

Since East Asia generously agreed to the southern tour, the Singapore Chinese Basketball and Volleyball Association has been preparing the competition schedule. For the convenience of the process, special committees were established, such as the East Asia and Singapore Track and Field Performance Committee, to handle all matters.

Numerous Cities in the South Seas Request Performances

Since the team's arrival, it has caused a sensation in the South Seas. Various cities have sent letters to Lin Aimin, chairman of the Singapore Chinese Association, requesting performances. To avoid disappointing overseas Chinese, the East Asia team has agreed to all requests. After performing basketball and track and field events in Singapore, they will go to Penang, Perak, Taiping Batu, and other places. When they appear, the audience is always packed. They greatly admire the team's artistry.

Track and Field Competition Sets National Record

At 1 PM on the afternoon of the 17th, the East Asia Singapore Men's and Women's Track and Field Performance Competition was held at the Singapore Amateur Football Association Stadium. There were over 1,000 spectators. Unfortunately, a light rain before the start dampened the audience's interest, otherwise, the entire venue would have been packed. Eight men's teams participated, but the results were mediocre. In addition to East Asia, twenty-one women were selected from Nanyang Girls' High School, Chinese Girls' High School, and Singapore Women's Sports School to participate for fun. East Asia has the nation's top athletes, and their results are far beyond what the women's teams in Nanyang can achieve. Miss Qian Hangsu, famous throughout the country, was injured in the ball game, greatly affecting her results. However, she still attended with her injuries, and the audience praised her excellent posture. In total, East Asia won first place in nine events. Chen Shuqing's 100-meter time of 13.4 seconds broke the national record, which was especially commendable. The overall results are as follows:

The Trip Was Not in Vain, Returning North with Great Reputation

In various performances, the East Asia team members' clothing is simple, their attitude is sincere, their skills are excellent, and their sportsmanship is exceptionally noble. They have no trace of the habits of current athletes, which gives the women of Nanyang a very deep impression. All sectors feel that the team's long journey across the ocean has been rewarding and they have experienced great hardship, so they have sent silver shields, velvet flags, etc., to commemorate the occasion. The team is scheduled to depart in early June and is expected to return to Shanghai on the 26th.
