Tripartite Meeting: Detailed Record of the Implementation Procedures for Children's Year

April to End of July is the Preparation Period, August to End of July Next Year is the Implementation Period, August to End of October Next Year is the Concluding Period

Representatives from the Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Education, and Ministry of Industry met at the Ministry of Education at 9 AM on the 19th to discuss the implementation sequence of the National Children's Year and the budget for the implementation committee. Chen Tun and Wei Erzhuang from the Ministry of Interior, Chen Panzao, a counselor from the Ministry of Education, Wu Yanyin, the chief of the department in charge, senior specialists, and Fan Shou from the Ministry of Industry, Zhang Chongde from the Ministry of Health, etc., were present. Wu Yanyin chaired the meeting, and Xue Tianhan took the minutes. (1) The implementation procedures for the National Children's Year were revised and approved, and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval before being promulgated. (2) The organizational regulations for the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, resolved last week, were re-amended and approved, and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review along with the implementation procedures. (3) The budget for the National Children's Year Implementation Committee was discussed, the various expenditure amounts were agreed upon, and will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. Regarding the implementation procedures for the National Children's Year, it is said that the preparations will begin when the National Children's Year Implementation Committee is established in April this year. Therefore, the first preparation period is set from April to the end of July this year. The second implementation period is from August of this year to the end of July of next year. The third concluding period is from August 1st to the end of October next year. As the implementation of Children's Year will last for a year (until the end of July next year), the implementation committee must handle the concluding matters such as investigation reports and compiling publications during the three-month period from August to October next year. The members of the Implementation Committee are jointly composed of the Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Education, and Ministry of Industry, and members will also be appointed from the Central Propaganda Department and the Sanitation Committee.

Ministry of Education Orders Completion of 23rd Year Vocational School Survey Form

(Nanjing, 20th) The Ministry of Education ordered various departments and bureaus that the survey form on the general situation of vocational schools in the province for the 22nd year, which was previously filled out and sent to the ministry, has been compiled by the ministry. Now that the 23rd year is about to end, the general situation of various vocational schools this year urgently needs to be re-investigated. Therefore, the ministry has prepared a form and issued an order to the departments to immediately forward it to the schools, ordering them to comply with the instructions on filling out the form and report it to the ministry within the time limit for verification. The forms without school names are for newly established schools or schools that have not been verified by the ministry. Furthermore, the ministry will conduct a survey once every year before the end of the year to observe the progress of each school and to inform them accordingly.

Ministry of Education and Others Send Personnel to Inspect Major Meetings in Lu, Ping, Jin, and Other Provinces

(Nanjing, 20th) The Ministry of Education ordered the appointment of specialists Sun Guozhou, Section Chief Xie Shuxin, and Zhu Zhanggeng, director of the Health Education Department of Central University, to go to Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Henan, Shandong, Shanxi, Hebei, Pingjin, and other provinces and cities along with Li Xien of the Northeast Youth Relief Bureau to inspect higher education. Sun, Xie, and Zhu are scheduled to go to Jinan on the 21st to inspect Qilu University before going to Ping to inspect public and private universities. From Ping, they will go to Tianjin, Hebei, Shanxi, Hubei, Anhui, and other eight provinces and cities for inspection, which will take about two months before returning to Beijing.

The Municipal Education Bureau Sets Examination Methods for Normal School Graduates

Implementing Rules for the Examination Committee, Ordering All Normal Schools to Comply

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order yesterday to public and registered private normal schools and secondary schools with attached normal courses, stating: "Regarding the graduation examinations for students of normal schools, the Ministry of Education previously promulgated the Provisional Regulations for Graduation Examinations of Normal School Students, which this Bureau copied and forwarded for compliance. Subsequently, various normal schools and secondary schools with attached normal courses in this city repeatedly presented difficult circumstances, and this Bureau, based on the situation, obtained approval to postpone the examinations to the second semester of this year. Now, this Bureau has formulated the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's Measures for Graduation Examinations of Normal School Students in the Second Semester of the 23rd Year, and the Implementing Rules for the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's Examination Committee for Graduation Examinations of Normal School Students. In addition to submitting reports to the Municipal Government and the Ministry of Education for review and record, we are hereby urgently issuing the regulations and rules, announcing them in advance, and ordering your school to comply accordingly. This order."

Letters from Xiao Yishan, Liu Qiao, and Others Praising the "Ten Professors' Manifesto"

Xiao Yishan Praises It as the Gospel Amidst National Decline; Liu Jieao Emphasizes the Impermissibility of Hesitating at the Crossroads

Recently, figures in domestic academic circles have paid close attention to the "Ten Professors' Manifesto." The China Social Problems Research Association in Nanjing has already initiated a series of Cultural Construction Symposiums, inviting Chen Lifu, He Bingsong, and 24 others to participate in discussions. Lin Liru, Dean of the Teachers College of Guang Dong Qinqin University, and Yang Lianggong, a supervisor of the Supervisory Yuan, also expressed to others that the principles of the manifesto are indeed unassailable, but hope that the ten professors who signed the manifesto can have further performance in how to achieve its realization so it is not just empty words. In addition, Xiao Yishan, professor of history at Peking University, and Liu Jieao, an economist studying in Berlin, recently wrote to their friends, mentioning the issue of China-centered cultural construction, and also expressed their expectations. The huge influence of the "Ten Professors' Manifesto" is even more evident. Attached below are the letters from Xiao and Liu:

Xiao Yishan's Letter: "You and other gentlemen lead the masses and construct a China-centered culture, which is truly the gospel amidst national decline. Looking up to the road ahead, I am filled with admiration. Mr. Lifu also discussed this matter in the past, believing that culture essentially has no distinction between East and West, old and new. From the perspective of their similarities, the round head and square feet are no different. From the perspective of their differences, the states of Qin and Yue also have different interests. Therefore, nature is the same and principle is also the same, customs are different and techniques are also different. Techniques have refinement and crudeness, so it is okay to learn from each other. Principles have no differences, so why must we imitate? Previous people were ignorant of the source of learning, and thus had the mistakes of self-imposed closure and blind imitation. Recently, the atmosphere has slightly shifted, but I am afraid that those who are rigidly attached to the past may be equivalent to the faults of recklessness and dismemberment. In the 18th year of the Republic, I founded the College of Literature, History, and Politics, with the aim of promoting Chinese culture. Although the influence was great at the time, the results were small, and I had long anticipated that there would be today. However, how can we revive the extinct and continue the interrupted, so that the false does not confuse the true? I hope you can add to this idea."

Liu Jieao's Letter: "Recently, I read in the newspaper about the manifesto issued by you and other gentlemen. After carefully examining it, I was pleasantly surprised. Recalling my days in Europe, I often discussed the issue of Eastern and Western culture with several friends, all of whom believed that our country's cultural policy, after hesitating at the crossroads and being deeply poisoned, urgently needed a re-examination, a change of strategy, and a new beginning. After returning to China, I gathered many like-minded people and loudly appealed to seek advice from domestic scholars. Unexpectedly, the ten professors' manifesto completely coincided with the intentions of myself and others. This proves that the truth is where everyone has the same feeling. During my two years in Europe, I realized from my daily observations that although Western culture has its advantages, if we disregard our national conditions and transplant them one by one, the result will not only not help the current difficulties, but will also be the source of the demise of our Chinese nation. Fortunately, you and other gentlemen have made a high-profile call, and the whole country has responded. From now on, we will change course and move towards the future of a national-centered culture. I know that in a few years, the whole country will definitely have a thriving atmosphere. I have no in-depth research on this issue, but my intuitive understanding may also be of reference. If I have spare time, I plan to write an article to seek opinions."

Essay Contest Organized by the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association

The Municipal Education Bureau Orders Teachers and Students of All Schools to Participate

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice yesterday on behalf of the Anti-Tuberculosis Association, announcing an essay contest with prizes and urging teachers and students of all schools to participate. The announcement stated: "Tuberculosis is harmful to life and it is urgent to find ways to prevent it to maintain health. The China Anti-Tuberculosis Association is aware of this and has specially formulated a concise essay contest charter and is widely soliciting submissions. This Bureau should support this effort. We hereby announce this to all teachers and staff in municipal and private (registered) primary and secondary schools in this city for their information. Students above the middle school level are also welcome to participate. Please forward this notice for their information. Attached below is the Concise Essay Contest Charter of the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association. The China Anti-Tuberculosis Association Essay Contest Charter: Preamble: Tuberculosis has been harmful for a long time. People lack common sense and are ignorant of prevention. Therefore, those who get sick and sacrifice their lives each year number in the millions, which is a major cause of weakness for our nation. In order to popularize tuberculosis prevention education and enable people to have a considerable understanding, our association has specially issued a 'Anti-Tuberculosis Vanguard' publication and is soliciting works with prizes. The concise charter is described below: 1. Any citizen of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, age, or social status, may participate. 2. Topics: (1) The relationship between the tuberculosis prevention movement and the Chinese national rejuvenation movement; (2) Tuberculosis prevention and education; (3) From the perspective of the Chinese national physique, talk about the tuberculosis prevention movement. (Choose one of the three topics.) 3. Prizes: divided into three types: First prize: 50 yuan; Second prize: 30 yuan; Third prize: 20 yuan. 4. Essays must be at least 500 characters long, and can be written in classical or vernacular Chinese, but must be written clearly in Chinese characters, and use modern punctuation marks. Please also indicate the mailing address at the end of the manuscript. 5. Submissions that have been disclosed elsewhere will not be accepted. Manuscripts must be sealed with the author's personal seal for verification when claiming the prize. Those without a seal will be rejected. 6. Submissions must be received by the end of March 1935. Late submissions will not be valid. Selected submissions will be notified by special letter and announced in this publication. 7. This association has hired Niu Huisheng, Li Ting'an, Yan Fuqing, Zhu Hengbi, Weng Yunlong, Ding Fubao, and Wu Liande as judging committee members. Once a judgment has been made, no objections will be accepted. 8. Regardless of whether submissions are accepted or not, they will not be returned. If you must have your submission returned, please state this in advance and include sufficient postage. 9. Submissions should be sent to the Editorial Department of the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association, No. 41, Chihong Road, Shanghai. 10. If there are too few submissions or a lack of good works, the deadline may be extended and the prize amount may be reserved."

Youth Circles Plan to Organize the National Customs Society

For the purpose of connecting feelings and studying academics, several dozens of people in the youth circles of this city, including Sun Yucai, Guo Zengcheng, and Shen Qiyan, have initiated the organization of the National Customs Society. After being approved by the municipal party headquarters to organize, the second meeting of initiators was held yesterday, and it was resolved that (1) the draft of the society's charter was approved, (2) members will be sought, (3) a preparatory office will be set up at No. 29 Xinjiang Road, (4) a founding assembly will be held regularly when preparations are mature, (5) Guo Zengcheng and Sun Yucai will be promoted as guiding directors, and (6) Shen Jiyan, Cheng Ming, Huang Yaqiang, Cao Jingting, and Lin Ronghui will be elected as preparatory committee members.

Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

Contribution Speech

Review of National Goods Exports

— Yang Mang

The fate of national goods this year is plagued by the decline of the rural economy internally, and pressured by the global economic recession externally. The path is becoming narrower and narrower, which is undeniably true. However, the rebirth of national goods in Southeast Asia is indeed the only way out. Our national goods manufacturers should unite to promote the export of national goods. According to the returning Southeast Asian investigators, the biggest difficulties in promotion are: exchange rates, transportation, insurance, etc., all of which are controlled by others. The heavy interest on mortgage loans and the losses suffered by tariffs are relatively inferior. National goods are lagging behind in every aspect. This is a matter that the national goods industry should quickly think of ways to use national unity to open up this export path, which is not to be delayed. The reporter believes that in addition to the above problems, there is one of the most important things that the national goods industry has not paid attention to and has long lost the trust of overseas Chinese merchants in Southeast Asia, which is the lack of selection of goods. General vendors arbitrarily transport shoddy goods to Southeast Asia in the name of national goods. These overseas Chinese merchants initially purchased them with enthusiasm, but what they bought were inferior goods, which not only became short-tempered, but also became discouraged. They are the real enemies of national goods. Therefore, I believe that in the future, our national goods manufacturers should jointly form an inspection agency through the same industry association, recruit experts, and use their technology. All export goods must undergo strict inspection and careful review in order to restore lost credibility and open up new paths for the future. This matter is extremely important and should not be solely dependent on the government, regarded as a formality, or well-intentioned but entrusted to the wrong people, turning it into a source of profit. Mr. Zhang Gongquan said: "To promote national goods, everyone must work hard in the future and do it themselves." This is indeed what our national goods industry should pay attention to.

National Goods Movement Goes to the Family

— Quan Jia

In the current era, I believe that the only way for national goods is to use economic methods to achieve the most effective results! What is the economic method? ——The national goods movement goes to the family!

Three or four years ago, when I went to the countryside, I often saw women making straw hats as their side business. If this method is used in the manufacture of national goods, then the results will be very significant. Because ordinary national goods factories must build steel-concrete factory buildings before manufacturing goods, and hire many office staff. If these expenses are eliminated, there is only one way to bring the national goods movement into the family!

A friend who studied in Japan told me that the reason why Japan's light industry is so developed is because their costs are low. Why are their costs low? Government protection is certainly a major reason, but the development of family factories is the biggest reason.

Then some readers may wonder, now is the machine world. If the family industry method is implemented, I am afraid that the handicraft industry will be revived. Isn't this a step backward?

I believe that family factories do not only use manual labor. Machines can also be used, but that requires two or three households to cooperate. Moreover, what I am talking about is small industry. When it comes to large-scale industries, it is necessary to set up factories! But large capital is run by the country. Let me give you an analogy: In the struggle between national goods and foreign goods, large industry is like artillery, heavy machine guns, and small industry is like rifles and hand grenades. In the current economic downturn in China, I hope to add more rifles and hand grenades, and we will choose the convenient ones to do! The organization of family factories is the meaning of this!

I saw a women's magazine talking about the decline of Chinese women. Bourgeois women are anesthetized in singing and dancing halls, middle-class women are gambling and having fun at home, and there are still many Noras wandering in the wrong path, working as vase-style female clerks. Are women really declining? Quickly come back from the path of extinction and take the path of family factories!

This year is the Student National Goods Year. I hope the education community will seriously promote this and encourage this major task of "family factories"!

Group Wedding and Promoting National Goods

— Zhang Mengzhao

The first New Life Group Wedding Ceremony in Shanghai will be held at 3:00 PM on April 3rd in the auditorium of the Shanghai Municipal Government. Fifty-eight young men and women will get married under the goal of thrift. This is truly a groundbreaking and unprecedented event! At the same time, our country's famous Maya Silk Factory is taking advantage of this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity to specially weave men's and women's silk dress styles for the general groom and bride. The male dress gown material is priced at 15 yuan for Grade A and 12 yuan for Grade B. The female dress material is priced at 5 yuan and 6 jiao for Grade A and 4 yuan and 5 jiao for Grade B. The veil rent is 1 yuan and 5 jiao per set. After inspecting the prices, they are still considered cheap. In addition, in order to promote domestically produced silk, it has been approved by the Social Affairs Bureau. I think that not only men's and women's dresses can take advantage of this opportunity to achieve great results! Other items such as Sanyou Society's Hehuan pillows, towels, menstrual belts, children's bibs, as well as men's Zhongshan suits, Xiaohuayuan's women's shoes, Family Industry Society's Butterfly Cream, etc... can be advertised at half price and sold to the young men and women in the group wedding. It is tantamount to jointly promoting group weddings on the one hand, and effectively promoting national goods, reducing imports, preventing the outflow of silver, and quickly selling national goods at low profits! The impression of national goods on young men and women is getting deeper and deeper. Why wouldn't merchants be happy to do so?

Things That the National Goods Industry Should Pay Attention To

— Ba Ling

When it comes to promoting the national goods movement, I believe that consumers should naturally make their best efforts to use and purchase national goods. However, from another perspective, the national goods production industry should also seize the opportunity to use this to establish a psychological foundation for national goods production that will forever be believed by the Chinese people. In this way, consumers and producers will cooperate practically. Then, our Chinese national goods movement will naturally achieve good results and reach the point of success. This is a certain truth. I think everyone should understand this very well!

However, it is unfortunate that after years of the national goods movement and the unanimous advocacy and publicity from top to bottom, producers and consumers seem to be more aware. However, as I see it, there are still two things that the national goods production industry should pay attention to and should really pay attention to (the things that consumers should pay attention to are not within the scope of discussion in this article, so I will not mention them much). Because this has a great influence on the future of the entire national goods movement, I will write about it below for discussion with the national goods production industry!

(1) The same industry should abolish the policy of cheap competition - The same industry and the same industry should have been united. How to study promotion methods? How to determine the price of goods! This should be discussed with the same industry in advance. However, what is the current situation of the national goods production industry? Alas! Besides cheap competition and internal strife in the same industry, what else can be said? This is a very serious crisis. An industrialist said: "Cheap competition is the death of national goods." It is truly sincere! I hope that the same industry and the same industry will quickly wake up and organize the same industry group or the same industry association, or joint business office to remedy this shortcoming. For example, the match industry has organized a joint association, and the enamel industry also has a joint business office. Recently, the steel product industry and the seasoning industry have also established the same industry group and the joint business office. This is a very good phenomenon, which can avoid internal strife and the occurrence of cheap competition in the same industry. I think: Other industries in the national goods production industry really need to pay attention urgently.

(2) Production should absolutely avoid shoddy production. To gain the trust of consumers in national goods, the first thing to do is to make the goods reliable. What is reliable means that there is absolutely no shoddy component mixed in. This is also a very important thing. Regarding the future of goods promotion, it is very important and large. The national goods production industry in our country has been able to pay attention to this, but there are still some producers who cannot avoid shoddy production. This should be very careful) This matter is not only related to the psychology of consumers. At the same time, it can also cause a bad impression among the same industry. From a broader perspective, it has a great impact on the sacrificial national goods movement. At this time when the national goods movement is flourishing, the author hopes that the national goods production industry will pay close attention to it.

The author believes that the above two points are what the national goods production industry should actively pay attention to at present. Therefore, I am using the position of the National Goods Weekly to study with the production industry.

Visitation Notes

Investigation Notes on Kunming Winery

— Ji Yu

Opening history, Chinese people have had a glorious page in industry. Silk tea porcelain etc. all held the highest position in the world in the past. We can admit that Chinese people are smart and hard-working. This cleverness and hard work can open up a promising road for industry as long as the bad habits of conservatism are eliminated.

In an era where these conservative bad habits are still growing luxuriantly, it is really not easy to see a factory that is thoroughly reformed and seeks progress, but now I have actually seen a Kunming Winery.

The Kunming Winery is located on Kunming Road and covers a large area. Currently, they only produce soy sauce temporarily. There were a total of five people who went to visit this time, based on a friend's introduction.

Following the doorman, we stepped into the reception room. Then, a Mr. Mao came to greet us. We sat in the reception room for a while, and then visited various places under the guidance of Mr. Mao.

The first place we arrived at was the laboratory. There, at the appropriate temperature, many types of yeast were cultured in various instruments. Mr. Mao told us: "Yeast is very important for making soy sauce. This kind of bacteria is like workers, doing the most important and impossible step for us. The distilleries do not select the best type of yeast from among the many types of yeast to use, but simply expose the raw materials to the air, allowing any type of bacteria to take on the manufacturing duties, so the products cannot be improved. This house of ours is an important work to find the best kind of bacteria other than the soy sauce made by chemical experiments.

Secondly, Mr. Mao led us to the fermentation place. It was a series of narrow and long houses. The temperature was very high. Wooden shelves were placed on both sides, and wooden trays were placed in the trays, all filled with the raw materials that were fermenting,——beans. Fermentation will release carbon dioxide gas, and because it is convenient for fermentation, there are only two ventilation holes left, so we came out in a short time, and then went to a very large house.

This room is special. It is all made of cement large square tanks, with walkways between the tanks. There is an empty tank in one corner of the room, so Mr. Mao pointed to it and said to us: "After the fermentation is completed, salty brine is obtained by using specific gravity, and it is first placed in this tank, and then put down these fermented beans. There is a pipe inside the tank, which is connected to water vapor. The water vapor has a temperature of 100 degrees Celsius, which is high enough than the temperature of ordinary sunlight, so we make soy sauce. We do not need to expose it to the sun like in distilleries. In addition to the fact that flies and dust will not mix into the soy sauce and hygienic conditions are obtained, we can still use water vapor to pass through this pipe at night to make the output rapid."

Walking out of this room and turning the corner, we saw a huge hydraulic press. Using a hydraulic press can squeeze out more soy sauce than the old-fashioned press. Their costs are also lower because of this. According to Mr. Mao, their soy sauce is now sold well not only in this city but also in other cities such as Hankou. In the future, they will also make wine.

When we walked out of the Kunming Winery, I kept thinking in my heart: Chinese people are smart and can work hard. This cleverness and hard work can open up a promising road for industry as long as the bad habits of conservatism are eliminated.

Historical Materials on National Products

— Sun Chouchang

The electric fans used in the past were all imported goods. Since the Hua Sheng Electric Appliance Factory manufactured its own electric fans, their effectiveness has surpassed that of imported goods, while their price is much lower. Therefore, Chinese people all advocate using domestic products, which saves a considerable amount of financial resources each year. The founder of the factory, Mr. Yang Jichuan, had not studied electrical engineering before entering school. All his electrical knowledge was obtained through his talent, and the results were even better than those of students who studied abroad. This shows that our country's industrial technology is not inferior to others, but unfortunately, no one promotes it. Therefore, I am publishing in this journal the five-character律 poem and preface presented to him by his elder brother, Yang Yuzhan, the other day, which he recorded in the tenth month of 1927, regarding Mr. Jichuan's new invention of electric fans, to add luster to the national products industry.

When I was young, I stayed at home and had not studied Western learning. Later, I went to Shanghai for trade and bought a book called "Essentials of Electricity" to learn gilding for amusement. Unexpectedly, this led to a sudden realization, and I understood the science of electricity thoroughly. I also naturally understood Western mathematics without a teacher. So I founded an electrical appliance factory in Hongkou, Shanghai, named Hua Sheng. Not only did I make many inventions in electricity, but I also understood the subtle details of various machines as clearly as if I were looking at a fire. Not only were foreign engineers inferior to me, but also foreign students who knew me often wrote letters to ask for my guidance. In the past, electric light factories were often stolen of electricity, but there was no way to investigate or prevent it. Later, I invented a limiting meter, which eliminated this drawback, and now all electric light factories benefit from it. Recently, I invented a fan that saves more electricity and has stronger power than imported products, while also reducing the price. As a result, it sells well in all provinces, and we cannot supply enough. There are many other inventions, all of which have been effective. Was I born with this knowledge? Or did I learn it? I cannot decide. The poem says: "The machine's heart is not used at all, and one gains complete success in learning from the ancients. This path must be given by heaven; who else is like you? Holding a cup, I ask the moon from afar; lying on a mat, the wind arises by itself. How many new things I have seen! My thoughts in the clear river are endless."

Introducing Wuxi's Yuan Grass Carpets

— Lü Bin

From an economic standpoint, with the current bankruptcy of Chinese rural areas and the decline of cities, all industries are withering, and a gloomy atmosphere permeates our surroundings. Advocating the purchase and use of domestic products, developing national production, and promoting national capital are the urgent tasks, the essential strategies for economic recovery, and the major actions to save the crisis. However, although general domestic products come from domestic factories, most of the raw materials still need to be purchased from foreign merchants. As a result, they have to go through another layer of exploitation, and the price is inevitably more expensive. It is still somewhat difficult for the people when purchasing power is weak. Naturally, it is best to use domestic raw materials to manufacture purely authentic domestic products.

The farm of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Institute in Wuxi, in view of the economic decline of our country's rural areas, should urgently seek salvation. In addition to improving seeds and planting methods for crops, it also promotes rural side businesses, such as rural crafts, which are also an important part. At the same time, it trains students in these skills and directly teaches the general public in various public education experimental areas, with remarkable results. All raw materials are domestic products, which avoids heavy exploitation. And the cost can be reduced, and sales are easy and widespread. For example, the yuan grass carpets are manufactured with extraordinary sophistication, with many patterns, and are very elegant for laying in halls and living rooms (see picture). The author specially visited Mr. Guo Yiquan, a rural arts and crafts teacher at the Institute, yesterday and was told the following:

"The Rural Arts and Crafts Training Institute of our institute's farm and the Rural Arts and Crafts Training Institute jointly established with the Beixia Public Education Experimental Area teach rural villagers and women to use their spare time to carefully make various brick-shaped carpets. The raw material is yuan grass from Hushu Pass, Suzhou, which is completely authentic domestic product. Whether it is a Chinese-style hall or a Western-style living room, using this kind of carpet as an embellishment is not only beautiful but also durable and useful. As for the size, it can be made according to the buyer's wishes. Now that we are shouting for rural revitalization, our work may be beneficial!"

When Mr. Guo talked to me, he immediately took out the finished yuan grass carpets for me to see. There were various patterns, and the yuan grass was dyed in red, blue, green, yellow, and other colors. It is said that each square foot is priced at only eighteen cents, which is many times cheaper than foreign felt carpets!

I heard that the Wuxi Civilian Vocational Training Center also produces this kind of yuan grass carpet, and many people in the market use it. I would like to introduce it here together, hoping that patriotic gentlemen and those who promote domestic products can buy and use it more, wouldn't it be possible to slightly supplement the national economy?

Free Talk

Talking About Foolish Hard Work

— Jiang Jiping

In Daudet's "Letters from My Mill," I saw many excellent essays. One of them, "Master Cornille's Secret," describes the tenacity and indomitable spirit of a flour miller, which can well represent the spirit of Westerners' foolish hard work. He said that when France's industry was not developed, when steam engines had not yet been invented, many mills used wind power to grind flour, so hard-working people could obtain abundant food and clothing. Every Sunday, the mill owners happily took out fragrant wine to entertain guests, and the housewives were also dressed beautifully, wearing golden crosses, and everyone played the flute and danced. But later, people from Paris came to that place and established a steam flour mill. The wages were cheaper, and the flour was ground faster, so everyone sent their wheat to be ground there. This robbed a lot of business from the windmills, so everyone could not maintain their business and closed their doors one after another. Some went to do other businesses, and some became destitute. The mill owners could no longer take out fragrant wine to entertain guests, and the housewives no longer had leisure time to dress up. This lively place suddenly became unusually desolate. Among these closed mills, only one was still open, and its windmill was still circling in the sky. This was Master Cornille's mill. It wasn't just for a day, everyone suspected whose wheat was being brought to him to grind? But Cornille was very diligent, every day he drove a donkey carrying two bags of wheat and sent it to his own mill, but he didn't let anyone in. Even when he wasn't in the mill, he kept the door tightly closed, as if he was afraid that someone would steal a grain of his wheat. Unexpectedly, one day, he forgot to close his mill door, and several children went in to take a look. There was no wheat there. The original book describes the expressions of these children when they first entered the mill very well. It says: "Strange! The milling room was empty, there wasn't a single bag, not a single grain of wheat; there wasn't any flour dust on the walls and spider webs, and even the warm fragrance of crushed wheat that was usually in the mill couldn't be smelled. The grinding bed was covered with dust, and the big skinny cat was sleeping on it. The inner room also had the same atmosphere of abandonment and poverty: a broken bed, a few sets of broken clothes, a piece of bread on the stone steps, and three or four broken bags in a corner, with some lime and powder soil leaking out of the bags." Cornille's secret was discovered. It turned out that what his donkey was carrying was lime. The children spread this secret throughout the village, and the old flour miller sat in his mill and cried. It turned out that he worked so hard to do this in order to win some glory for the mill. Everyone was moved by his sincerity and sent wheat to him to grind. After that, the mill continued to operate until Cornille died, and then the windmill of the mill stopped. In our view, what he did was close to madness, or a kind of mental illness caused by excessive stimulation, but in fact, it was a very strong will, a spirit of resistance. Many Western scientists and entrepreneurs have succeeded because of this kind of foolish spirit. This is not affectation, not foolishness, but strong effort. When Chinese people encounter failure, they think that there is no hope at all, sacrifice everything, and become depressed for the rest of their lives. When they encounter people doing such foolish hard work, they even laugh at them, so they never succeed. This article seems like a joke, but it really inspires us a lot.

The Valley of Miasma

— Wu Yan

It was only the second month of the lunar calendar, but the weather in the valley was terribly hot and stuffy, as if it were already the hottest days of summer.

The reeds by the roadside were thick and hard, and if you weren't careful, they would simply prick your legs and feet.

Although flies don't eat people, when you see them suddenly pounce on your face, you feel afraid, as if they are going to bite off the flesh on your face.

At that time, I was taking wandering travel as my main form of entertainment, so when I walked to such a place, of course, I felt particularly interested. I planned to slow down my pace and use curious eyes to search and gather some things that I had never seen before. However, my travel companion, whom I had met on the mountain road the day before, a suspicious fellow who claimed to be a businessman but had no goods, showed a fearful look. He turned his head, wrinkled his thick eyebrows, and urged me:

"Walk faster! Walk faster!... Do you know what place this is?"

"Of course, I know. ... What kind of flower is that?... Don't worry, will anyone rob you or me?"

I had long guessed that in this place with steep mountains and dangerous valleys, bandit grandpas were inevitably present to some extent. A vagabond with empty hands, what was there to worry about, only caring about staring blankly at a tree three or four zhang tall that was all red flowers near by.

"Ghost flowers!... I'm telling you, I'm not talking about those who rob people, young man!"

He pulled the package that was approaching his waist up to his back, took a few steps, and then answered me in a tone that was almost scolding, as if he were an old man, but he was actually only about thirty years old. I couldn't help but feel a little unhappy. I still walked slowly, glancing casually at the roadside, saying something that was not quite a question:

"Then,... what is there to be afraid of?... Are you afraid of not being able to reach the shop before dark?"

"Humph, haven't you heard people say? There's miasma in this valley.... Hurry up, hurry up, it'll come out when it gets dark...."

"Ah!"

He heard me exclaim in surprise and spoke energetically, as if to make me admire his experienced words even more.

"People say that the miasma in this valley is released by a toad spirit, understand? A toad spirit. On rainy days, the horse drivers have seen it, guess, hey, wait a minute, guess, what does it look like?"

He even stopped and began to quiz me.

"Let's go! Isn't it just an ugly big toad?... Have you forgotten the miasma?"

I waved my hand at him, as if urging him to hurry forward.

His feet immediately and instinctively sped up, but his mouth was still speaking excitedly.

"A big toad? No! A beautiful girl in red clothes! Standing on the roots of a yellow fruit tree, combing her black hair, combing it, mom, how charming!... "

"Why don't we go see her tonight? Such a charming thing!"

Not really believing these kinds of things, I said something to tease him.

"Um, are you not afraid of losing your life!... Those who can see her, how can they still live?"

"What? Does she eat people?"

"She doesn't bother to eat you! You haven't even gotten close to her, and you'll be poisoned by the miasma she spits out!"

"Then, how do you know she's a woman in red clothes?"

"Hey, didn't I tell you it was someone else who told me?"

"What! Is he still alive? Didn't you say that if you saw her, you would die?"

"Ha, how can you be so stupid? He also heard it from someone else!"

I didn't like continuing the playful questioning, because human beings are inherently good at lying and also good at believing lies, so I silently admitted that I was stupid.

"Also, the miasma of Lujiang Dam is different."

He bent down to tidy up the loose straps of the straw sandals on his feet. When he straightened up, he began this sentence, but he didn't go on, as if waiting for me to urge him: "Then what is it like?" However, I didn't speak, only caring about burying my head and continuing on my way.

"I'm telling you, it's a black fish spirit in the river...."

He finally continued to speak. In my heart, I thought: "Thank you, I didn't ask you to tell me!" He spoke as he walked, and unconsciously slowed down. Sometimes, if I didn't tell him to hurry up, he would stop on the road and let his mouth move alone.

The mountains around the valley were very high. By mid-afternoon, the sun had disappeared long ago, leaving only the unbearable stuffy heat. We both unbuttoned our buttons, opened our chests, and let the sweat from our wet shirts escape. I was afraid that I wouldn't be able to reach the mountains to stay overnight tonight, and that I would have to spend the night outdoors in the valley, and let the miasma torment me, so I repeatedly turned back and urged him:

"It's getting dark, walk faster, wouldn't it be better to talk about it at the shop over there?"

"Okay, okay." (To be continued)

A Visit to the Oriental Culture Institute (Part 2)

— Lan Ru

The first thing we saw was the antiquities exhibition room on the third floor.

Walking into this room was just like walking into the Palace Museum in Beiping. There were ancient coins, ancient costumes, ancient tiles, ancient mirrors, ancient hairpins, ancient swords, ancient bricks... from various dynasties in ancient China, everything that one could wish for. Books that they copied according to ancient Chinese versions were displayed here, including "Wen Xuan," "Historical Records," "Book of Rites," "Mao Shi," "Confucius' Family Sayings," etc. Among the many picture albums, I discovered a picture album titled "Commemorative Publication of the Manchurian National Fengtian Museum," and immediately all the blood in my body boiled up, as if I had been greatly insulted, and I had no intention of turning the pages any further.

After coming out of here, we visited the book storage room.

This was a seven-story book storage building. Although each floor was only about twenty shop mats in area, the equipment inside was too strange! The bookshelves were all steel, and the stairs, floorboards, and surrounding walls were all iron. It is said that the reason for building it like this was entirely for fire prevention.

Because the Research Institute had only been established for a year, there were not that many books stored inside. Many bookshelves were empty. The gentleman told us that the total number of books currently stored was only 70,000, half of which were Chinese books, just 35,000.

Originally, one could take the elevator to the book building, but because we wanted to visit, we had to trouble our two legs. When everyone's footsteps came into contact with the iron stairs, they made a piano-like sound, which was extremely interesting. Everyone quietly listened to this rhythmic music and forgot the fatigue of going upstairs.

On each floor, there was a young man in his twenties sitting there writing book slips or sorting books. When he saw us, he always stood up and smiled and bowed to us. The Japanese people's research spirit is really admirable. Some ancient books that were so rotten that they had no words were completely new after they were copied by them. They used uniform covers for binding, which looked very neat and beautiful.

After visiting the painting library, we were led to the ancient book reproduction office and the photography room. The camera used was the latest Japanese model, like a microscope, which could magnify something as small as a speck of dust to a few feet, which made it very convenient to reproduce ancient books.

Later, we also visited the conference room, the joint research room, the lecture room, etc. In the joint research room, we saw regular publications from various universities in China, as well as "Jiu Tong," "Twenty-Four Histories," and maps of various provinces in China. The gentleman also told us that a Chinese gentleman named Ba Xiangyin was teaching them Chinese for two hours every week.

It is said that there are also certain restrictions on the researchers here. Those who are not doctors are not qualified to come to study. The chairman of the board is Hattori Unokichi. Including the directors and staff of the office, library, and photography department, there are a total of more than 40 people. The salary of each person is at least 110 yuan per month and at most 300 yuan. The research topics are different for each person, and the time when the research starts and ends is also stipulated. They are currently studying: the study of "Chu Ci" literature, the material culture of ancient northern ethnic groups in China, the study of the Liao and Jin dynasties, the study of Confucian governance, the study of "Zuo Zhuan," the history of medieval Chinese currency, and the history of thought in the Wei, Jin, Southern and Northern Dynasties.

The Kyoto and Tokyo Research Institutes publish one volume of the "Oriental Studies Report" every year, and most of the content is the research reports of the researchers.

On the way back, everyone was silent, lowered their heads, and walked quietly on the small stones. I thought that everyone's minds might be filled with more thoughts than small stones, but there should be one thing in common, right?

"Why have all of China's cultures gone into their libraries?"

People and Books

— Han Feng

Goldfish

Because the children like goldfish, I also seem to have developed a bit of interest in this aspect. However, the children do not know how to raise goldfish, and I, from morning to night, am walking around without stopping. Therefore, the goldfish that come to my house either turn from "alive" to "dead" or from "vermilion" to "white." This has happened more than once. In addition, there is another danger: one of the children is very fond of dissecting creatures. Of course, he is not willing to let go of the goldfish lightly. Often, when no one is in the hall, he secretly takes the live goldfish out of the tank and takes it to the ground outside the door, where he slowly dissects it with a small knife all by himself. No matter how much you try to persuade him, it is always ineffective. Since last year, we have no longer raised goldfish, although whenever I see goldfish carriers or pass by goldfish stalls, I still want to move the idea. Not long ago, in a used bookstore, I saw a manuscript from the Kangxi period, titled "Classic of Red Fish," written by a Suzhou man who studied the life of goldfish for 30 years. It divides goldfish into 56 major categories, scientifically explaining each category and writing many methods for raising goldfish and collecting their eggs, etc. Due to the past relationship with goldfish, and because this book has no printed version and the asking price was only 40 cents, I bought it. Later, Mr. Zhenduo came south and saw this manuscript. He also said that he had never seen a printed version and proved from the changes that it was the original manuscript, and I was even more interested.

The Beiping Triangle Love Tragedy Murder Case

— Meng Ruo

The number of disputes arising from love among modern Chinese youths is truly countless. Those that go unnoticed are naturally impossible to know. The number revealed daily by newspapers is already unbelievably high. The seriousness of this issue in male-female relationships is very worthy of attention.

Recently, another triangle love tragedy occurred in Beiping, with very serious circumstances. From all perspectives, this cannot be said to be anything other than an unfortunate social reality. The murderer in the tragedy, Liu Jinggui, is a student at Beiping's Beihua Art School, 24 years old, from Xuanhua. In 1932, he fell in love with the physical educationist Yu Ming (also from Xuanhua, 34 years old, a graduate of Shanghai Jiaotong University) and they got engaged. Subsequently, during the North China Games, he met Teng Shuang (from Zhaoyang, Hunan, 29 years old, a graduate of Beiping Women's Normal University). Consequently, in the spring of 1933, he broke off the engagement with Liu and married Teng. Liu harbored deep resentment as a result, and this time, he killed Teng to vent his anger.

When we slightly research the whole story of this tragedy, we immediately feel that the blame for the tragedy really focuses on Yu Ming alone. The reason is that Yu was originally a man with a wife, yet he subsequently fell in love with two women, and both times got engaged. He treated love and engagement as a child's play, a fact that is very obvious. Since Yu was unwilling to grow old with his first wife, and then fell in love with Liu Jinggui, he should have divorced his first wife and married Liu, and everything would have been resolved. But Yu was naturally fond of the new and tired of the old, and disregarded his engagement with Liu, and fell in love with Teng Shuang again, and proceeded to get married. Therefore, Liu felt unwilling and harbored thoughts of revenge, and resolutely came out and killed Teng to resolve his long-held resentment. Therefore, in the creation of this tragedy, Yu cannot escape primary responsibility.

As for Liu Jinggui's behavior, it is also inevitably too extreme. Since Yu had already been engaged to Liu, and then married Teng, then Liu's abandonment was Yu's fault, not Teng's; this reasoning is very clear. Now, Liu committed this crime, killing Teng. His mistaken behavior is also unforgivable. Furthermore, since Yu fell in love with Teng, he already intended to abandon Liu, so he discussed breaking off the engagement with Liu. If Liu had been unwilling to break off the engagement at the time, he could have legally and vigorously negotiated with Yu. But since Liu didn't do this, and readily agreed to cancel the agreement, then Liu could also allow them their freedom and go find his own way out. Then nothing would have happened. Who knew that Liu's lingering affection was not broken, he resented Yu extremely, and ultimately resolved to kill Teng to vent the resentment in his chest. Liu's crime of intentional homicide is also deserved.

The one deserving our sympathy is Teng Shuang alone. She was sacrificed at the hands of a rival in love because of love disputes, which is really very unjust. However, Teng was not cautious enough in engaging in a relationship with Yu earlier, and there is inevitably some fault. Perhaps this is the source of her death today.

Private Diary of a Woman

— Cheng Quan

Thinking repeatedly for an entire night, my nerves felt like they were being pounded by a sharp, stubborn iron pestle. When the turmoil was intense, my heart felt like it had been shattered by a dumdum bullet. Throughout the night, amidst the crowing of chickens and the ticking of the clock, I pondered and pondered. Then, a final determination drove me: at dawn, I decided to leave.

What else could I do but leave? In this rotten social stratum, when the economic foundation, which is the main tool for human liberation, still rests solely with men, the fate of women being toyed with and humiliated is ultimately unavoidable. But, unbearable humiliation and being toyed with are the most potent spiritual poisons for humans with special inspiration.

Could it be that when the times have developed to the forefront of the twentieth century, when humans are flaunting their own culture, there are still people who consider playing with women who have grown up in an unreasonable society and lost their economic ability as reasonable, pleasurable, and pleasing to the eye?

It's really something that makes people think about it for three days and nights, what kind of era is this? What kind of era is it? Is it civilized, cruel, or so insignificant that it can hardly be recorded on a page of history, a bizarre era that cannot be seen?

The riddle of this bizarre era is only known by ghosts!

However, no matter what, it's simply impossible to endure insults that humans cannot endure.

(Perhaps it's because I recognize a few characters: perhaps it's because of the oppression of adolescence, which is most prone to crime? When I broke away from the old shell of the so-called "family" in a corrupt and stubborn atmosphere, I had no chance to consider, and was pushed into the wild waves of society.

What greeted me was the clamor, insults, and the attacks of hunger, which is one of the instincts of mankind, between people.

Then a caring friend said to me!

—In this society, it is impossible for a woman to escape the shame of being toyed with and find a piece of bread or two to chew; women are most likely to starve to death, but women are also most unlikely to starve to death—like you, you are young, and with your youthful smile, you can already exchange it for luxurious enjoyment and have more than enough. Why do you have to suffer the pain of hunger under the deceptive slogan of "independence"? Fool!

But, I am young, with a hot, clean, and bright-loving heart. I have the courage to control my life. So I refuted my friend's words with youthful enthusiasm and condemned them as cowardly and humble.

Is the world really like that? Who believes it?

However, whether you believe it or not, the facts finally gradually unfolded. Several experiences of aimless wandering, insults, and hunger scared me. Finally, in a spirit of self-abandonment, like countless weak women, I took marriage as a job to relieve hunger, and sold my youthful smile, soul, and body wholesale in exchange for a rotten heart and the continuation of life.

When I was first caught in someone else's hands, I was perhaps being toyed with out of kindness(?): but later, because the other person had money, the other person had the mentality of a "young master": so, in times of displeasure, in times of turmoil, in times of boredom, in all times when it was not appropriate to pretend to be charming, I began to be scolded like a slave.

—Bitch! Cheap thing!

And for example, yesterday, because I didn't smile in a way that catered to the other person's preferences, I was slapped!)

And this slap may end my life, but it may also help me start a new life?

Suicide? Why bother? Suicide under the golden "young master" is more shameful than any humble act. So, I thought for a night and decided to leave at dawn.

But: where to go?

When will the sky brighten?

Passing Through Zhenjiang

— Hua Mu

Taking the train through the tunnel, this is the second time. The first time was on the Guangzhou-Kowloon train, the length of the tunnel is similar to that of Dougai Mountain. When the train rumbles towards the entrance of the tunnel, you stretch your head forward to look, the train becomes a gliding snake spitting out black gas,

Page 21

in an agile posture, swiftly drilling into the entrance of the tunnel. At this time, the nerve endings will feel a strange sensation coming over, like suddenly falling from the bright world into a bottomless abyss, the body losing its support. If there are also children in the carriage, then you can still see their innocent and childish state of clapping and cheering. After a while, the light reappears, and you can't help but turn your head to look back, at this time the train has become a snake coming out of the cave.

When the train comes out of the Dougai Mountain tunnel, you will know that Zhenjiang has arrived. First, you see Jiaoshan, and then, the tower on Jinshan Mountain, which rises into the clouds, grabs your attention. At this time, if you are a person with a bit of a poetic temperament, and you know a little about the story of the White Snake and Xu Xian, you can't help but stir up infinite nostalgia, gazing far away at the tower in a daze. You will recall and imagine the mysterious White Snake and the Zen master Fahai's battle of magic and ability, a sad, magnificent, and beautiful scene.

When the train starts to move forward again amidst the sound of the whistle, you can only bid farewell to Jinshan from afar with a look containing infinite sympathy, regret, and mourning.

Human nature is, after all, not completely poisoned by cruel and ruthless etiquette. You think, the story of the White Snake can spread among people, be enjoyed by people, grab the sympathy of countless people, and move the tears of countless single men and women, isn't this a manifestation that human nature has not been completely poisoned by cruel etiquette?

This tragic and beautiful White Snake Legend contains how many women's tears. This is not a myth, nor a fictional novel, this is a bloody and vivid real tragedy of the struggle between love and etiquette. The Snake Maiden is not a snake, not a demon, she is a human being with blood, flesh, and soul, a supremely complete woman. That sanctimonious Zen master Fahai is a man-eating monster in human form.

However, the evil forces of etiquette are ultimately too great, and its gates are ultimately difficult to shake; all the efforts, struggles, and resistance of the White Snake Maiden have completely turned into bubbles, and the result is still a complete defeat. The suppression under the Leifeng Pagoda declared the death penalty of the love of the supreme woman! And this ancient tragedy, the inherent deficiency in human nature, is left with bloody traces as a story of sympathy, regret, and sadness for the world.

Sister-in-Law Zheliu

A Person Shaped by Emotion

— Zong Xin

Still feeling lost, but the whole body feels much lighter. A fugitive!

Walking to the edge of the Saigon coast, I suddenly felt that the surroundings were so vast that my body was a little shaky; it felt like I had just escaped from prison! Standing under the tall and huge French postal ship, looking up, my mind became even more cheerful and rushed forward, and I couldn't help but exhale a long breath. A little lingering fear trembled slightly towards that terrible shadow.

The white clouds in the sky are boundless for thousands of miles, and I seem to be about to lightly fly to the vast and longed-for distance! I mustered up the courage to board the French postal ship. Looking at the long and winding ninety-nine bends of the Saigon port, the green port water, the green grass on both sides, and the light posture of the tropical style, my heart throbbed in bursts.

But turning back to look at Saigon, my heart was a little trembling, mixed with a sad and sour taste. The tearful appearance of my brother flashed back in my mind:

"What else is there to say? What else is there to say? I have wasted half my life's efforts."

My brother worked hard to create me, but I have been imprisoned once or twice. How could my brother be willing to let his younger brother drift alone to the vast distance! However, the younger brother is absolutely not content with this dead,沉, life-and-death merchant life, but wants to risk pursuing so-called freedom! My brother will never understand, he is simply seeking death!

For the past few days, my brother has been unable to eat. Why must my younger brother leave! And my eyes, also withered, dared not look at my brother's body. Alas, humanity shaped by emotion! I can't stop trembling with sadness, and a fire-like heat surging, a unbearable battle, making it impossible for me to swallow food in my throat.

Leaning on the side of the ship, I thought about it until my eyes went dark, and waves of dark shadows flickered. Saigon seemed to be shrouded in tear-like beads of fog, as miserable and sad as an autumn night with a sad wind and bitter rain. The crying sound of my brother's sobbing was always trembling in my ears, that sorrowful appearance…

My eyes went deep into Saigon, an inexplicably vague gaze!

Suddenly, a person whom I knew well walked over from afar. I rubbed my confused eyes and my heart jumped. But until he walked up to me, I was still stunned. He didn't call me, but took a roll of banknotes from his pocket and said to me:

"Your uncle gave it to me, told me to bring it to you. Your uncle told you that after you get to Hong Kong, you should take a first-class cabin back to Shantou and be careful on the way." He glanced at me and seemed to be leaving.

I don't know why, but I completely fainted. My whole body was trembling, my arms were so sore that it was difficult to lift them, and my eyes were wide open and speechless. The sour tears in my eyes were gushing out. A sense of awareness was telling me: if my brother called me back again, how could I say no to going back? I left so resolutely, but my brother still loves me so much! My whole body seemed to be immersed in a gentle embrace, and emotion was soaking through my cold bones! At this time, my brother was the master of my iron-like will! Although I finally left, the great power of will saved me! But the magic of kinship overwhelmed me again after I left! It is a person shaped by emotion!

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Darryl F. Zanuck on Methods of Choosing Material

— Goldfinch

The most important issue for a film is its material. The most crucial task for filmmakers is finding suitable material.

This may seem like a commonplace observation, but when this statement comes from the head of an American film production company, such as Darryl F. Zanuck, head of production at 20th Century Fox, it is noteworthy. According to Zanuck, human emotions such as joy, anger, sorrow, and happiness are eternally constant. Therefore, whether in the era of Sophocles in ancient Greece or the time of Shakespeare, the driving forces in drama, such as terror and hope, retain their ability to evoke sadness or joy today, just as they did in ancient times. Thus, discovering new stories for the screen, fresh and moving stories, involves seeking a new subject matter and simply reconfiguring and arranging the emotional elements. This applies not only to the screen but also to the stage and novels.

In fact, the skills of arranging and constructing dramatic stories are mastered by all successful authors, but filmmakers must do more than simply rearrange and interweave a story. Here, a more important question arises: the issue of "time and taste." "A magazine editor," Zanuck says, "can start editing a magazine for December in mid-July. They can put a snow scene on the cover and fill it with winter reading material. That's simple and risk-free. But in film production, it's not that easy. What material can we choose that we anticipate will suit the audience's taste six months from now?"

"You can't possibly guide popular tastes. To try to lead people in this film business is a dream, because the public refuses to be led by anyone. But if you run after the public, that's extremely dangerous. In a trend, only the first film can succeed. The rest of the imitations are like dwarfs watching a play behind giants. But how to predict future trends, the trends of audience thought, is a most important and complex issue."

How to predict future trends, how to grab the first big wave, and ride it to shore? This isn't about leading public opinion but rather providing something that the public needs at a particular time when they need it. Success in filmmaking is like success in baseball. Two moving objects must meet at a specific point in space and time. On the baseball field, those two objects are the ball and the bat; but in the film industry, the two objects are the material and the public's taste. In either case, if you're too late, too early, too broad, or too weak, you'll miss the opportunity and fail.

"What do you base your predictions of public taste on?" someone asked Zanuck.

Zanuck said, "I use newspapers. I read newspapers from all over the country every day. Two years ago, while reading the newspaper, I felt that American audiences were gradually growing tired of gangsters. Before that, American audiences admired gangsters. They admired that kind of chivalrous behavior, helping the weak and subduing the strong. But they soon realized that the rampant lawlessness of gangsters was a great scourge to society. So I started constructing 'Public Enemy,' which for the first time fully exposed the cruelty and depravity of these gangsters. Sure enough, when this film came out, the public flocked to it. Similarly, 'The House of Rothschild' would have been impossible to make even a year earlier. But later, I felt that the American people had developed a great interest in the activities of bankers in international diplomacy, so I decided to make that film. As expected, after the film was made, it was warmly welcomed by the public."

Someone asked him, "Will future films be adaptations of Shakespeare's plays or stage operas brought to the screen?"

Zanuck replied: The level of the audience's taste is constantly increasing, so it is certainly possible to adapt Shakespearean works for film in the future. It's just a matter of time, as people generally enjoy profound dramas, immersing themselves in them, rather than just showing off their status. As for bringing opera to the screen, that's an even greater step forward, not only because of the convenience of set changes but also because the singers in opera only need to have clear and accurate voices, not necessarily ones that resonate throughout the heavens. This means that opera singers on the screen can be slimmer than opera singers in the opera house and don't all have to be enormous in girth.

Film Reviews

Review of "Mills of The Gods"

—— Da Guangming

As a reflection of the American economic panic, "Mills of The Gods" is not without value from various perspectives. Naturally, we cannot ignore that this reflects Roosevelt's New Deal and actively supports Roosevelt's political views through film art. Precisely for this reason, the concerned cannot help but be exposed to the impact of the global economic panic on American industry. It uses charts to illustrate that the prosperity index of American industry reached its peak in 1929 during the relatively stable period after the war. However, after the start of the economic panic, it immediately plummeted rapidly, and even large factories on the verge of bankruptcy had to close their iron gates. As a result, workers' strikes and riots could no longer be suppressed, causing great pain. Therefore, after Roosevelt took office, the New Deal—a desperate measure among desperate measures—came into being.

However, the playwright does not refrain from distorting reality at all. For example, he emphasizes the decadent lives of the capitalists. The children and grandchildren of the old boss, Mary, are all lazy and pleasure-seeking, indifferent to their own industries. We do not deny the decadent lives of the capitalists, but this cannot be the main reason for the failure of their industries. Similarly, he has the factory owner's daughter and the worker's leader fall in love, and the unrealistic nature of this cannot hide its deceptive effect. Because of these distortions of reality, he later presents a deceptive conclusion: on the one hand, sympathizing with the workers' actions, when the factory director closes the factory to avoid further losses, the workers surround the factory, almost rioting. At the same time, he tries his best to protect the interests of the factory owners. For example, because the factory owner's daughter and the worker's leader had a one-night stand of kindness, the worker's leader tries to ease the labor unrest. When it can no longer be eased, the factory owner orders the police to shoot. Finally, he has the factory owner's son accidentally killed by police machine gun fire as a kind of punishment (although he would never let him die at the hands of the workers, but rather accidentally by his own force). And the old factory owner's wife, who has been running the factory for more than fifty years, takes out another four million gold to revive the factory. As a result, the workers are very grateful, and there is so-called labor-management compromise and capable cooperation. Regarding this point, its political deception is extremely obvious, but when we examine the results of the New Deal, it is not very successful. On the contrary, it makes the United States more and more restless. Thus, the didactic effect of this film is equivalent to wasted effort.

However, as mentioned above, this film expresses the didactic effect by dividing it up and expressing it separately. Whether it is the script, actors, or cinematography, they are all very capable and quick, especially the excellent director, Roy William Nell, who handles every scene very delicately and meticulously. Particularly exquisite is the scene where the factory owner's daughter goes to the worker's leader's house, when describing the love and desire between them, that kind of delicate psychological description is indeed beyond ordinary mediocre directors. In addition, when using indexes to express the decline in production, he uses sound effects and quickly organizes many facial close-ups. This superior technique is, in any case, an expression of film art. Because of things like this, we do not undervalue this film, although it inevitably has a certain degree of social deception.

A scene from "Jin Lian's Ordeal"—Joan Park and James Dunn co-star—Showing in Nanjing Today

Prelude to "A Beautiful Heart"

— Jin Wen

Since Japanese imperialism occupied our Northeast, several years have passed. At the time of the "January 28th" and "September 18th" incidents, people were once full of anti-imperialist enthusiasm. I remember that Chinese films also made several anti-imperialist films, but as of today, public sentiment seems to be declining day by day, and Japanese imperialism's policy of actively invading our country still exists. The recent special change in Chahar is a clear demonstration.

In order to arouse the anti-imperialist enthusiasm of the people, the Star Film Company produced an anti-imperialist film "A Beautiful Heart" with the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army as the background. The film is directed by Xu Xinfu and stars Hu Die, Wang Zhengxin, Xu Xinyuan, Gu Meijun, and Gu Lanjun. The story depicts how a patriotic warrior escaped from the prison of Manchukuo and how he stubbornly resisted the Japanese army in the ice and snow. In this story, the protagonist, the leader of the Volunteer Army, Li Feng (Wang Zhengxin), how he defeated the Japanese army in a difficult environment and finally died on the battlefield. Interspersed with a romance, tragic and ardent, making people want to cry without tears and want to laugh without sound after watching it. Undoubtedly, this is a film that awakens the people's anti-imperialist enthusiasm. May readers come and see this heartbreaking picture. (But)

"The Merry Widow" Makes a Comeback

— Bei Lin

The biggest romantic musical extravaganza produced by MGM during 1934-35, "The Merry Widow," was originally a fragrant and romantic stage play. Recently, MGM spent a lot of money to bring it to the screen.

The story of this film describes the wealthiest widow in the Kingdom of Mechavi, Sune, who is very young, beautiful, romantic, and good at singing and dancing. When she gets together with Count Donilo, a charming young man who is also a skilled socialite and a member of the Imperial Guard, many fragrant and romantic things happen. In the story, such as Donilo climbing over the wall late at night to introduce himself to Sune, and the later scenes where the two turn against each other due to misunderstandings, are very moving. But the greatest scenes in it are probably the music and dance. There is a most beautiful song, "Merry Widow," which is said to be now sung by almost every young person at home and abroad.

The director is someone we all know, Liu Renqian. As for the leading actors, Hivrely and McDonald, they are even more familiar to us, so there is no need to introduce them.

"The Merry Widow" was shown for many days in a row at the "Nanjing" a few weeks ago, and now, due to the demands of the majority of the audience, it has been re-released at the "Lido" starting yesterday.

Film Novel

Clive of India (6)

— Mao De

Manning looked at the ragged soldiers marching off and sighed, "This is truly the work of madmen." Cand said, "It really is a madmen's team." Pemberton said, "And, if you ask me, the officer in charge is also a madman." Governor Pigot, who was standing beside him, seemed to disagree, saying, "Fortunately... there is such a madman."

The goddess of fortune favored this desperate venture. After a few months, this small army of ragamuffins, or madmen, had become a large army. It was unstoppable, and no one who stood in its way was spared. Finally, the siege of Delhi-Napore was also lifted. Clive had become a victorious general, the conqueror of South India, and everyone had to take notice when he returned in triumph.

Amid the bombardment of Fort St. David, a grand welcome party was being held at the Governor's office. Civil and military officials were all present, quietly awaiting the arrival of the honored guest. But everyone became doubtful; where had the honored guest gone? Edmund McGreene reported, "When we returned, he left the main group, taking only ten guards, to go to a nearby place to tear down a French war memorial. He said that would let the Indians know the military power of the British." General Townsend, upon hearing this, said quickly, "That's right, that's right, that makes a lot of sense. But... will he come to the welcome party here..." Edmund said quickly, "He said he would come. He wouldn't not come. But, I want to ask for a leave to pick up my sister. She just arrived here from England today." The general quickly agreed, "Go quickly, go quickly."

Margaret was talking to Captain Clarke. Clarke was happily recounting many battlefield stories. One day, Clive was wounded in the head, but he disarmed a French unit all by himself. "He shouted at them to throw down their weapons. He told them they were trapped in the core. It was so dark that they couldn't see anything around them. So they were so panicked that everyone threw their weapons on the ground. By the time we found out and went to help him, he had already lined up a group of prisoners and marched them off. We all laughed so hard we almost died!" He said, laughing wildly.

Edmund walked up and said, "Ready? Let's go." Margaret suddenly became afraid and said, "Has... has... he come?" Edmund said, "No. He just has to go directly to the welcome party by himself. What would he look like after galloping forty miles? I wanted to have him meet you here and go with you." Margaret suddenly cried and said, "I... I... don't want to see that person!" Edmund said strangely, "What's wrong? Everyone in India wants to see Robert Clive today!"

Margaret pleaded, "Don't you understand what I mean? I came to this place... just wanting to meet an ordinary clerk... a friend of yours. Now he is a big man. He must think that I want to marry him." As she spoke, she sobbed and cried. Edmund laughed, "Margaret, it's too late to back out now! If Robert wants to see you, he must see you. If he wants you to marry him, he will tell you. You haven't even met him yet!"

Margaret said, "I want him to know that I have no hope at all." As she was speaking, there was already a commotion outside. Needless to say, Clive had arrived. Margaret's face turned red with anxiety. Her heart was pounding wildly, as if it wanted to jump out of her chest. She begged Edmund, "Tell him that I've already left!" But Edmund didn't look back and ran out to greet Clive. (To be continued)
